كتاب الحج
شرائط الوجوب
على الفور بشرط حرّيّة وبلوغ وعقل وصحة وإسلام وقدرة زاد وراحلة فضلت عن مسكنه عند أبي يوسف وهو الأصح فلا يجب على المجنون فلا يجب على الكافر أي وبشرط قدرة وعن ما لابد منه ونفقة أي وبشرط قدرة وعن مؤونته أي وفضلت والمصنف لم يميز بينها . صفة قدرة - من غير شروع والوجوب إنما كان بالآية السابقة، ثم اعلم أن الركن في الحج شيئان: الوقوف بعرفة، وطواف الزيارة أي ،معظمه وواجباته خمسة: السعي بين الصفا والمروة، والوقوف بمزدلفة، ورمي الجمار، والخروج عن الإحرام بالحلق أو القصر، وطواف الصدر، وعد بعضهم الواجبات نيفاً وعشرين والضابط أن كل ما يجب بتركه دم فهو واجب وما عدا ذلك إما سنة أو أدب بأن يتوسع في النفقة، ويحافظ على الطهارة، وعلى صون لسانه، ويستأذن أبويه ودائنه وكفيله، ويودع المسجد بركعتين ومعارفه ويستحلهم، ويلتمس دعاءهم، ويتصدق بشيء عند خروجه، ويخرج يوم الخميس أو الاثنين أو الجمعة. (عيني، فتح) بشرط حرية فلا يجب على العبد. (عيني)] اعلم أن الشروط منها شروط وجوب وشروط أداء وشروط صحة، مع حذف بعضها، فشروط الوجوب العقل والبلوغ والإسلام والحرية والوقت والاستطاعة والعلم بكون الحج فرضاً، وشروط الأداء: صحة البدن وزوال الموانع الحسية وأمن الطريق وعدم قيام العدة في حق المرأة وخروج الزوج أو المحرم معها، وشروط الصحة الإحرام بالحج وأشهر الحج والمكان المخصوص، فلا يجب على العبد مطلقاً مدبراً كان أو مكاتباً أو مأذوناً؛ لعدم أهليته لملك الزاد والراحلة، ولا على الصبي ولا على المعتوه. (فتح) وبلوغ فلا يجب علي صبي. وصحة [ الجوارح، فلا يجب على مقعد غني وزمن غني. (عيني)] أي بشرط صحة الجسد، فلا يجب على الأعمى ولو وجد قائداً، وهو مذهب الإمام ، وكذا من الشروط أن لا يكون محبوساً ولا خائفاً من سلطان، ولا يجب على الزمن والمفلوج ومقطوع الرجلين وإن ملكوا الزاد والراحلة، هذا في ظاهر الرواية عن أبي حنيفة، وهو رواية عنهما، وفي ظاهر روايتهما يجب الحج على هؤلاء إذا ملكوهما، وهو رواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة والخلاف مبني على أن الصحة من شرائط الوجوب أو الأداء، قال الإمام بالأول، وهما بالثاني، وفائدة الخلاف تظهر فيما إذا ملكوهما، فإنه لا يجب عليهم الإحجاج بمالهم عنده، خلافاً لهما إذا لم يقدر على الحج وهو صحيح، فإن قدر عليه ثم زالت القدرة وجب الإحجاج اتفاقاً. (فتح) وراحلة بالملك أو بالإجارة، لا الإعارة. (ط) فضلت عن مسكنه ومؤونته فلو كان له دار لا يسكنها ولا يواجرها أو متاع لا يمتهنه أو عبد لا يستخدمه وجب عليه أن يبيعه ويحج به ويحرم عليه أخذ الزكاة إذا كان قدر المائتين؛ لأنها فاضلة عن حاجته، فتحصل بها الاستطاعة، وقوله : عما لابد منه" يعني من غير المسكن كقضاء الديون، وإلا فالمسكن أيضاً مما لابد منه (فتح) لا بد منه من الثياب والفرس والسلاح وأثاث البيت والخادم وكتب الفقه إن كان فقيها. (ط،ع)

ذهابه وإيابه وعياله وأمن طريق ومحرم أو زوج لامرأة في سفر، فلو أحرم صبي أو عبد فبلغ أو أعتق فمضى لم يجز عن فرضه ومواقيت الإحرام .
أو أحرم الصبي أي العبد لخمسة وهو يعقل
ذهابه وإيابه: [ أي مدة ذهابه إلى مكة، ورجوعه إلى أهله راكباً. (ط، ع)] لا ماشياً مطلقاً، وقال مالك: يجب الحج على من له قدرة على المشي؛ لأنه مستطيع إليه بواسطة القدرة على المشي، ولنا أنه عليه فسر الاستطاعة بالزاد والراحلة، فيتعلق الوجوب بهما، وهذا في حق من كان بعيداً . عن الكعبة. وعياله : [ أي وقدرة نفقتهم وأولادهم الصغار إلى عوده. (ط)] ومن تلزمه نفقته، وإن لم يكن ذا رحم محرم منه، والمراد بالنفقة: الوسط من غير إسراف ولا تقتير، وليس من شرط الوجوب على أهل مكة ومن حولهم الراحلة؛ لأنهم لا تلحقهم المشقة بالمشي، فأشبه السعي إلى الجمعة. (فتح) وأمن طريق بالجر عطف على قدرة أي وبشرط أمن طريق ولو بالرشوة؛ لأنه لا يتأتى بدونه. (ط،ع)] فإن كان في الغالب السلامة يجب الحج وإن كان الغالب الخوف والقطع لا يجب ولو كان بينه وبين مكة بحر فهو كخوف الطريق، فإن كان الغالب في البحر السلامة من موضع جرت العادة بركوبه يجب وإلا فلا. (فتح، مسكين) ومحرم إلخ: أي لا تثبت الاستطاعة للمرأة إذا كان بينها وبين مكة مسيرة سفر إلا بمرافقة محرم أو زوج؛ لقوله عليه: "لا يحل لامرأة تؤمن بالله واليوم الآخر أن تسافر سفراً يكون ثلاثة أيام فصاعداً إلا ومعها أبوها أو ابنها أو زوجها أو أخوها أو محرم منها"، رواه مسلم وأبو داود وهو حجة على الشافعي حيث قال: يجوز لها الحج إذا خرجت برفقة ومعها نساء ثقات رمز الحقائق: ١٥٠/١] وقيد بمدة السفر ؛ لأنها يباح لها الخروج إلى ما دون السفر بلا محرم أو زوج، ولو وجدت محرماً ليس لزوجها المنع من حجة الإسلام خلافاً للشافعي، والمحرم من لا يحل له نكاحها أبداً أو رضاع أو مصاهرة، وشرط فيه أن يكون مأموناً عاقلاً بالغاً حراً كان أو عبداً كافراً كان أو مسلماً، ولو كان المحرم فاسقاً أو مجوسياً أو صبياً أو مجنوناً لا يعتبر؛ لأن الغرض لا يحصل بالفاسق والمجوسي، ولا يتأتى من الصبي والمجنون الحفظ ونفقة المحرم عليها. (مسكين، فتح) سفر: أي في مدته وهي ثلاثة أيام فصاعداً. (ط، ع) فلو أحرم هذا تفريع على ما مر من الشرائط. (مسكين فمضى أي أتى بأفعال الحج، ولم يجدد الإحرام للحجة المفروضة. (ط)
عن برحم : لم يجز فرضه [ أي فرض الحج ؛ لأن إحرامهما انعقد للنفل فلا يؤدى به الفرض (عيني)] فإن جدد الصبي الإحرام قبل الوقوف بعرفة صح وجاز عن حجة الإسلام؛ لأنه في هذا الحال من أهل اللزوم، أما العبد إن جدد الإحرام فلم يجز عنه؛ لأن إحرامه لازم فلا يمكنه الخروج عنه بالشروع. (مسكين، فتح) ومواقيت جمع ميقات، وهو الوقت المحدود فاستعير للمكان ومنه مواقيت الحج لمواضع الإحرام التي لا يتجاوزها الإنسان إلا محرما، وهي خمسة. (مسكين، ع)
The Book of Hajj. Conditions of obligation: immediately, conditioned by freedom, puberty, sanity, health, Islam, and ability (provision and mount) surplus over his dwelling according to Abu Yusuf and it is the most correct. So it is not obligatory upon the insane, not obligatory upon the disbeliever, i.e., conditioned by ability, and what is indispensable and expenses, i.e., conditioned by ability, and his family's maintenance, i.e., surplus, and the author did not distinguish between them. Description of ability: without beginning, and the obligation is only by the previous verse. Then know that the pillars of Hajj are two: standing at Arafah and the visitation circumambulation (Tawaf al-Ziyarah), i.e., most of it. Its obligatory acts are five: Sa'i between Safa and Marwah, standing at Muzdalifah, stoning the Jamarat, leaving ihram by shaving or trimming, and Tawaf al-Sadr. Some counted the obligatory acts as over twenty, and the principle is: every act for the omission of which a dam is required is obligatory, and other than that is either sunnah or adab, such as being generous in spending, maintaining purity, guarding one's tongue, seeking permission from parents, creditor, and guarantor, bidding farewell to the mosque with two rak'ahs and acquaintances, asking them to release him, seeking their supplication, giving charity upon departure, and leaving on Thursday, Monday, or Friday. (Ayni, Fath) Conditioned by freedom, so it is not obligatory upon a slave. (Ayni) Know that the conditions include conditions of obligation, conditions of performance, and conditions of validity, with some omitted. The conditions of obligation are: sanity, puberty, Islam, freedom, time, ability, and knowledge that Hajj is a duty. Conditions of performance: health of body, removal of physical obstacles, safety of the road, absence of 'iddah for women, and the presence of husband or mahram with her. Conditions of validity: ihram for Hajj, the months of Hajj, and the specific place. So it is not obligatory upon a slave absolutely, whether mudabbar, mukatab, or ma'dhun, due to his lack of capacity to own provision and mount. Nor upon a boy or a lunatic. (Fath) And puberty: so not obligatory upon a boy. And health of the limbs: so not obligatory upon a rich cripple or a rich chronically ill. (Ayni) i.e., conditioned by health of the body, so not obligatory upon a blind person even if he finds a guide, and this is the madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa. Also among the conditions is that one should not be imprisoned or in fear of a ruler. It is not obligatory upon the chronically ill, the paralyzed, or the legless even if they possess provision and mount. This is in the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah) from Abu Hanifa, and it is a narration also from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. In the apparent narration from them, Hajj is obligatory upon these if they possess them, and it is a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa. The dispute is based on whether health is a condition of obligation or performance. The Imam says the former, and the two say the latter. The practical benefit appears when they possess them: it is not obligatory upon them to perform Hajj with their wealth according to him, contrary to them. If one was unable to perform Hajj while healthy, then ability ceased, then performing Hajj is obligatory by agreement. (Fath) And a mount by ownership or lease, not by lending. (T) Surplus over his dwelling and his family's maintenance: if one has a house he does not inhabit nor rent, or goods he does not use, or a slave he does not employ, he must sell them and perform Hajj with the proceeds, and it is forbidden for him to take zakat if he possesses the amount of two hundred dirhams because it is surplus to his need, and thus ability is achieved. His saying: 'what is indispensable' means besides the dwelling, like debt repayment; otherwise, the dwelling is also among what is indispensable. (Fath) Indispensable are clothes, horse, weapon, household furniture, a servant, and books of fiqh if he is a jurist. (T, A) His going and returning, his dependents, safety of the road, and a mahram or husband for a woman on a journey. So if a boy or a slave assumes ihram and then reaches puberty or is freed, and then proceeds (completes Hajj), it does not suffice for his obligatory Hajj. And the miqats for ihram are five. Or a boy assumes ihram, i.e., the slave, for five, while he is sane. His going and returning: i.e., the duration of his travel to Mecca and his return to his family riding. (T, A) Not walking absolutely. Malik said: Hajj is obligatory on one who has ability to walk because he is capable of it by means of ability to walk. Our evidence: The Prophet (peace be upon him) interpreted ability as provision and mount, so obligation is attached to them. This applies to one who is far from the Ka'bah. His dependents: i.e., ability to provide for them and his young children until his return. (T) And those whom he is obliged to support, even if they are not mahram relatives. The intended meaning of maintenance is moderate, without extravagance or miserliness. It is not a condition of obligation for the people of Mecca and its surroundings to have a mount because they are not affected by hardship of walking, so it resembles the walking to Friday prayer. (Fath) And safety of the road: joined to 'ability' by the genitive, i.e., conditioned by safety of the road, even by bribe, because it cannot be achieved without it. (T, A) If safety is predominant, Hajj is obligatory; if fear and banditry are predominant, it is not obligatory. If there is a sea between him and Mecca, it is like fear of the road: if safety at sea is predominant from a place where sailing is customary, it is obligatory; otherwise not. (Fath, Miskin) And a mahram etc.: i.e., ability is not established for a woman if between her and Mecca there is a distance of travel except with the company of a mahram or husband, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'It is not permissible for a woman who believes in Allah and the Last Day to travel a journey of three days or more except with her father, son, husband, brother, or mahram.' Narrated by Muslim and Abu Dawud. It is a proof against al-Shafi'i who said: it is permissible for her to perform Hajj if she goes out with a group and with trustworthy women. (Ramz al-Haqaiq 1/150) And it is restricted to travel distance because she is permitted to go out for less than a travel distance without a mahram or husband. If she finds a mahram, her husband is not allowed to prevent her from performing the obligatory Hajj of Islam, contrary to al-Shafi'i. The mahram is one who is permanently forbidden to marry her by blood, suckling, or marriage ties. It is required that he be trustworthy, sane, adult, whether free or slave, disbeliever or Muslim. If the mahram is a sinner, a Magian, a boy, or insane, it is not considered because the purpose is not achieved with a sinner or Magian, and protection cannot be expected from a boy or insane. And the expenses of the mahram are upon her. (Miskin, Fath) Travel: i.e., its duration is three days or more. (T, A) So if one assumes ihram, this is a branch of what has passed of conditions. (Miskin) Then proceeds, i.e., performs the acts of Hajj, and does not renew ihram for the obligatory Hajj. (T) By a blood relative: it does not suffice for his obligatory Hajj, i.e., the obligatory Hajj, because their ihram was concluded for supererogatory (nafl), so it cannot be performed as obligatory. (Ayni) If the boy renews ihram before standing at Arafah, it is valid and suffices for the Hajj of Islam because at that time he is among the people of obligation. As for the slave, if he renews ihram, it does not suffice for him because his ihram is binding (lazim) and he cannot exit from it by commencement. (Miskin, Fath) And miqat: plural of miqat, which is the defined time, then borrowed for place. From this, the miqats of Hajj are the places of ihram that one should not pass except in ihram. They are five. (Miskin, A)
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is an expansive commentary on the conditions of obligation (shurut al-wujud) for Hajj, drawn primarily from the Hanafi school. The author begins by listing the core conditions: freedom, puberty, sanity, health, Islam, and ability (provision and mount) that is surplus over one's dwelling and essential needs, according to Abu Yusuf, which is considered the most correct view. The commentary clarifies that these conditions are for the obligation (wujub), not just performance (ada) or validity (sihha).

The text then discusses each condition in detail:
- Freedom: a slave is not obligated because he lacks full ownership of means.
- Puberty and sanity: a child or lunatic is not obligated.
- Health: Abu Hanifa holds that physical health is a condition of obligation, so a blind person or cripple is not obligated even if wealthy. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider health a condition of performance, so such individuals must send someone else (i.e., perform Hajj by proxy) if they have the means. The practical difference appears when they have wealth but cannot travel: according to Abu Hanifa, no proxy Hajj is required; according to them, it is required. If they were healthy and became unable, then proxy is obligatory by consensus.
- Ability (istita'ah): the provision and mount must be owned or leased (not borrowed), and surplus over essential needs like dwelling, clothing, household goods, and debts. If one has surplus wealth, he must sell it to perform Hajj. The people of Mecca and its surroundings are exempted from the mount condition due to proximity.
- Safety of the road: if the route is predominantly safe, Hajj is obligatory; if dangerous, it is not. Sea travel is treated similarly.
- For women: a mahram or husband is required for a journey of three days or more. The mahram must be trustworthy, adult, and sane. This is supported by a hadith and is a proof against al-Shafi'i, who allowed travel with a trustworthy group of women.

The passage then addresses a subsidiary ruling: if a child or slave assumes ihram and then becomes obligated (reaches puberty or is freed) before completing Hajj, their Hajj does not count as the obligatory Hajj unless they renew ihram after becoming obligated. For the child, if he renews ihram before standing at Arafah, it suffices; for the slave, even renewal does not suffice because his ihram is binding.

Finally, the miqats (places of ihram) are mentioned as five, though not detailed here.

The commentary is rich in intra-madhhab differences (Abu Hanifa vs. the two companions on health) and inter-madhhab differences (Hanafi vs. Shafi'i on women's travel, Hanafi vs. Maliki on walking ability). The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is generally the view of Abu Hanifa, except where noted.

Key Terms
لازم (lazim): Binding; once a slave enters ihram, it becomes binding and cannot be exited without completing Hajj.
إحرام (ihram): The sacred state for Hajj or Umrah initiated by intention and talbiyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a child (who is not yet baligh) performs Hajj and reaches puberty during the day of Arafah before standing at Arafah, what must he do for his Hajj to count as the obligatory Hajj?
A) Nothing; it automatically counts.
B) He must renew his ihram after Arafah.
C) He must renew his ihram before standing at Arafah.
D) He must repeat the entire Hajj the next year.

Key Takeaway
A child or slave's Hajj before obligation is nafl; only a child can convert it to fard by renewing ihram before Arafah.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
12 min
Conditions for Hajj Obligation
States conditions for Hajj obligation and disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five conditions for the obligation of Hajj according to the Hanafi school, explain the evidence for each, and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i and Maliki views on specific conditions.

Core Idea
Hajj is obligatory only when five conditions are met: provision, dependents, safety, mahram for women, and maturity.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq outlines the conditions (shurut) that must be present for Hajj to become obligatory (wajib). The author lists them and then expands on each, providing the Hanafi proof and responding to objections from other schools. Understanding these conditions is essential because without them, Hajj is not required, and performing it voluntarily before obligation does not fulfill the Islamic duty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five conditions
From the opening line, extract the conditions: going and returning (provision and mount), dependents, safety of road, mahram or husband for women, and the absence of being a child or slave at the time of ihram.
The condition of being adult and free is implicit; children and slaves are not obligated.
2
Examine the condition of istita'ah
Understand the Hanafi interpretation of istita'ah as provision (zad) and mount (rahilah) for those far from Makkah, and the Maliki counterargument that walking suffices. Note the Hanafi proof: the Prophet (peace be upon him) interpreted istita'ah as such.
For people of Makkah and its surroundings, the mount condition is waived due to lack of hardship.
3
Analyze the condition of safety
Safety of the road is judged by predominant likelihood: if the road is generally safe, Hajj is obligatory; if danger is predominant, it is not. Sea travel is analogous to land travel.
Even bribery is allowed if needed to ensure safety.
4
Understand the mahram condition
For women, a mahram or husband is required if the journey is a travel distance (3 days or more). The hadith from Muslim and Abu Dawud is cited as proof against the Shafi'i view that a trustworthy group of women suffices.
The mahram must be trustworthy, sane, and adult; a sinful, Magian, child, or insane person does not suffice.
5
Apply the rule for children and slaves
If a child or slave enters ihram and then becomes mature or freed and continues, it does not count as the obligatory Hajj. They must perform a separate Hajj after obligation becomes due.
This shows that the conditions must be met at the time of ihram for it to satisfy the obligation.

شرائط الوجوب
ذهابه وإيابه وعياله وأمن طريق ومحرم أو زوج لامرأة في سفر، فلو أحرم صبي أو عبد فبلغ أو أعتق فمضى لم يجز عن فرضه
أو أحرم الصبي أي العبد لخمسة وهو يعقل
ذهابه وإيابه: [ أي مدة ذهابه إلى مكة، ورجوعه إلى أهله راكباً. (ط، ع)] لا ماشياً مطلقاً، وقال مالك: يجب الحج على من له قدرة على المشي؛ لأنه مستطيع إليه بواسطة القدرة على المشي، ولنا أنه عليه فسر الاستطاعة بالزاد والراحلة، فيتعلق الوجوب بهما، وهذا في حق من كان بعيداً . عن الكعبة. وعياله : [ أي وقدرة نفقتهم وأولادهم الصغار إلى عوده. (ط)] ومن تلزمه نفقته، وإن لم يكن ذا رحم محرم منه، والمراد بالنفقة: الوسط من غير إسراف ولا تقتير، وليس من شرط الوجوب على أهل مكة ومن حولهم الراحلة؛ لأنهم لا تلحقهم المشقة بالمشي، فأشبه السعي إلى الجمعة. (فتح) وأمن طريق بالجر عطف على قدرة أي وبشرط أمن طريق ولو بالرشوة؛ لأنه لا يتأتى بدونه. (ط،ع)] فإن كان في الغالب السلامة يجب الحج وإن كان الغالب الخوف والقطع لا يجب ولو كان بينه وبين مكة بحر فهو كخوف الطريق، فإن كان الغالب في البحر السلامة من موضع جرت العادة بركوبه يجب وإلا فلا. (فتح، مسكين) ومحرم إلخ: أي لا تثبت الاستطاعة للمرأة إذا كان بينها وبين مكة مسيرة سفر إلا بمرافقة محرم أو زوج؛ لقوله عليه: "لا يحل لامرأة تؤمن بالله واليوم الآخر أن تسافر سفراً يكون ثلاثة أيام فصاعداً إلا ومعها أبوها أو ابنها أو زوجها أو أخوها أو محرم منها ، رواه مسلم وأبو داود وهو حجة على الشافعي حيث قال: يجوز لها الحج إذا خرجت برفقة ومعها نساء ثقات رمز الحقائق: ١٥٠/١] وقيد بمدة السفر ؛ لأنها يباح لها الخروج إلى ما دون السفر بلا محرم أو زوج، ولو وجدت محرماً ليس لزوجها المنع من حجة الإسلام خلافاً للشافعي، والمحرم من لا يحل له نكاحها أبداً أو رضاع أو مصاهرة، وشرط فيه أن يكون مأموناً عاقلاً بالغاً حراً كان أو عبداً كافراً كان أو مسلماً، ولو كان المحرم فاسقاً أو مجوسياً أو صبياً أو مجنوناً لا يعتبر؛ لأن الغرض لا يحصل بالفاسق والمجوسي، ولا يتأتى من الصبي والمجنون الحفظ ونفقة المحرم عليها. (مسكين، فتح) سفر: أي في مدته وهي ثلاثة أيام فصاعداً. (ط، ع) فلو أحرم هذا تفريع على ما مر من الشرائط. (مسكين فمضى أي أتى بأفعال الحج، ولم يجدد الإحرام للحجة المفروضة. (ط)
Conditions of obligation: his going and returning, his dependents, safety of road, and a mahram or husband for a woman in travel. So if a boy or slave enters ihram and then becomes mature or freed and continues, it does not suffice for his obligatory (Hajj). His going and returning: meaning the period of his going to Makkah and returning to his family, riding – not walking absolutely. Malik said: Hajj is obligatory on one who has ability to walk because he is capable by means of ability to walk. Our proof: He (the Prophet) interpreted capability as provision and mount, so obligation is attached to them, and this is for one who is far from the Ka'bah. His dependents: meaning capability of their expenses and his young children until his return, and those whose maintenance is obligatory upon him, even if not a mahram relative. The intended meaning of maintenance is the middle course without extravagance nor stinginess. It is not a condition of obligation for the people of Makkah and its surroundings to have a mount because they do not experience hardship in walking, so it resembles going to Friday prayer. Safety of road: meaning condition of safety of road, even by bribery, because it cannot be achieved without it. So if safety is predominant, Hajj is obligatory; if fear and robbery are predominant, it is not obligatory. If there is sea between him and Makkah, it is like fear of road: if safety in sea is predominant from a place customarily sailed, it is obligatory, otherwise not. And mahram etc.: meaning capability is not established for a woman if between her and Makkah is a travel distance except with a mahram or husband; due to his saying: 'It is not permissible for a woman who believes in Allah and the Last Day to travel a journey of three days or more except with her father, son, husband, brother, or mahram.' Reported by Muslim and Abu Dawud, and it is a proof against al-Shafi'i who says: It is permissible for her to perform Hajj if she goes out with a trustworthy group of women. And it is restricted to the travel period because it is permissible for her to go out for less than a travel distance without a mahram or husband. If she finds a mahram, her husband does not have the right to prevent her from Hajj al-Islam, contrary to al-Shafi'i. The mahram is one to whom marriage to her is permanently forbidden by lineage, fosterage, or marriage affinity. Condition is that he be trustworthy, sane, adult, whether free or slave, Muslim or disbeliever. If the mahram is a sinner, Magian, child, or insane, it is not considered because the purpose is not achieved with a sinner or Magian, and protection and maintenance of the mahram are not possible from a child or insane. Travel: meaning its duration is three days or more. So if he enters ihram: this is a branch on the conditions mentioned. And continues: meaning he performs the actions of Hajj and does not renew ihram for the obligatory Hajj.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof that lays out the conditions (shara'it) for the obligation (wujub) of Hajj. The author begins by listing five conditions: (1) provision for going and returning (i.e., having enough funds to cover travel expenses both ways, including a mount for riding for those far from Makkah), (2) provision for dependents left behind, (3) safety of the road, (4) for women, the presence of a mahram or husband, and (5) the absence of impediments like being a child or slave (since Hajj is not obligatory on them, but if they perform it before obligation, it does not count as the obligatory Hajj). The text then expands each condition. On the condition of transport, there is a dispute with Imam Malik, who holds that ability to walk suffices. The Hanafi proof (dalil) is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) interpreted istita'ah (capability) in the Quran as provision (zad) and mount (rahilah), thus obligation depends on them. For dependents, the text explains that one must have enough for their needs (in a moderate way) until his return. For safety, if the road is generally safe, Hajj is obligatory; if generally dangerous, it is not. Even sea travel is analogous. For women, the text cites the hadith prohibiting travel of three days or more without a mahram, which is a proof against al-Shafi'i, who permits it with trustworthy women. The passage then defines mahram and sets conditions: trustworthiness, sanity, adulthood; a sinful or Magian mahram is not valid, nor a child or insane person.

Key Terms
الاستطاعة (al-istita'ah): Capability to perform Hajj, interpreted as having provision and a mount.
محرم (mahram): A person to whom marriage is permanently forbidden due to lineage, fosterage, or affinity, and who is trustworthy, adult, and sane.
أمن طريق (amn tariq): Safety of the road; if safety is predominant, Hajj is obligatory; if fear of robbery is predominant, it is not.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT a condition for the obligation of Hajj?
A) Having a mahram for women traveling a journey of three days
B) Ability to walk if one cannot afford a mount
C) Provision for dependents left behind
D) Safety of the road

Key Takeaway
Hajj is obligatory only when five conditions are met; each condition is grounded in explicit textual proof and defended against opposing views.

Child or Slave Performing Hajj Before Obligation
Ruling on child or slave performing Hajj before obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether a child or slave's Hajj before obligation suffices as obligatory Hajj, and distinguish between the cases of child and slave regarding renewal of ihram.

Core Idea
A child's or slave's Hajj before obligation is valid as nafl but does not count as fard unless conditions are met.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq deals with a nuanced situation: a child or slave performs Hajj before the obligation falls upon them. Later, they become eligible (maturity or freedom). Does the previous Hajj count as the obligatory Hajj? The Hanafi school answers with a clear distinction, which we will unpack here.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories and initial ruling
The passage addresses two individuals: a child (who has not reached puberty) and a slave. For both, if they enter ihram and later become free or mature but continue without renewing ihram, the Hajj does not suffice for the obligatory Hajj.
The initial ihram is for nafl because the obligation was not present.
2
Understand the condition for the child
If the child renews his ihram after reaching maturity and before standing at Arafah, then it does suffice for Hajj al-Islam. At that moment, he is obligated and his new ihram is for fard.
The renewal must occur before Arafah; otherwise it remains nafl.
3
Understand why the slave cannot benefit
For the slave, even if he renews ihram after being freed, it does not suffice. This is because his original ihram was binding (lazim) and he cannot exit it by starting anew.
The binding nature of ihram prevents changing the category from nafl to fard.
4
Grasp the underlying principle
The key principle is that the intention and obligation status at the time of ihram determine the nature of the Hajj. An act begun as nafl cannot later become fard unless a new ihram is made when obligated.
This distinguishes Hanafi view from some others.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلو أحرم صبي أو عبد فبلغ أو أعتق فمضى لم يجز عن فرضه ومواقيت الإحرام .
أو أحرم الصبي أي العبد لخمسة وهو يعقل
فلو أحرم هذا تفريع على ما مر من الشرائط. (مسكين فمضى أي أتى بأفعال الحج، ولم يجدد الإحرام للحجة المفروضة. (ط)
لم يجز فرضه [ أي فرض الحج ؛ لأن إحرامهما انعقد للنفل فلا يؤدى به الفرض (عيني)] فإن جدد الصبي الإحرام قبل الوقوف بعرفة صح وجاز عن حجة الإسلام؛ لأنه في هذا الحال من أهل اللزوم، أما العبد إن جدد الإحرام فلم يجز عنه؛ لأن إحرامه لازم فلا يمكنه الخروج عنه بالشروع. (مسكين، فتح)
So if a boy or slave enters ihram and then becomes mature or freed and continues, it does not suffice for his obligatory (Hajj). And the timings of ihram. Or the boy enters ihram: meaning the slave, for five (conditions?) while he is sane. So if he enters ihram: this is a branch on the conditions mentioned. And continues: meaning he performs the actions of Hajj and does not renew ihram for the obligatory Hajj. It does not suffice for his obligatory (Hajj) – meaning the obligatory Hajj, because their ihram was contracted for supererogatory (nafl), so the obligatory cannot be performed with it. If the boy renews ihram before standing at Arafah, it is valid and suffices for Hajj al-Islam because at that time he is among those upon whom it is obligatory. As for the slave, if he renews ihram, it does not suffice for him because his ihram is binding and he cannot exit it by commencing.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement and a parsing exercise dealing with the case of a child or slave who performs Hajj before the obligation falls upon them. The author states that if a child (who has not reached puberty) or a slave enters into ihram and then, after performing the acts of Hajj, attains maturity or freedom, that Hajj does not count as the obligatory Hajj (Hajj al-Islam). The reason, as explained in the commentary, is that their initial ihram was for nafl (supererogatory) because Hajj was not yet obligatory on them. Therefore, the actions cannot fulfill an obligation. However, if the child (after becoming mature) renews his ihram before standing at Arafah, it does count, because at that time the obligation is present. For the slave, even if he renews ihram after becoming free, it still does not suffice because his original ihram was binding (lazim), and once he starts, he cannot change his intention to obligatory. This distinction highlights the Hanafi position on the effect of obligation status on the validity of the act for fulfilling the fard.

Key Terms
النفل (al-nafl): Supererogatory act; here used to describe the Hajj performed without obligation.
اللزوم (al-luzum): Binding nature; once ihram is entered for Hajj, it becomes obligatory to complete it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Valid and suffices as obligatory Hajj
B) Valid as nafl only
C) Invalid because original nafal acts cannot be changed
D) Must be repeated because renewal is not allowed

Key Takeaway
A child's Hajj before maturity can suffice as obligatory Hajj only if ihram is renewed after maturity and before Arafah; a slave's Hajj cannot be thus converted because his ihram is binding.

The Five Mawaqit and the Obligation of Ihram at the Miqat
Definition and description of the five mawaqit and rulings on passing them

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the five mawaqit and explain why the Hanafi school requires ihram for anyone passing the miqat, even for non-Hajj purposes.

Core Idea
Ihram at the miqat is wajib for all entering the Haram, not just for Hajj or Umrah.

This lesson introduces the five fixed locations for entering ihram (mawaqit) and the ruling that it is obligatory for anyone who passes them with the intention of entering the Haram, whether for Hajj, trade, or any other purpose. We will also examine the proof from the hadith of Ibn Abbas and the disagreement with al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five mawaqit and their locations
From the source, list the five miqat locations: Dhul-Hulayfah (for Madinah), Dhat Irq (for Iraq), Juhfah (for Syria/Egypt/Maghreb), Qarn (for Najd), and Yalamlam (for Yemen/India). Note their approximate distances to Makkah.
These are fixed by the Prophet and cannot be changed.
2
State the ruling: ihram is wajib for anyone passing the miqat heading to the Haram
The Hanafi position is that ihram at the miqat is obligatory (wajib) for any afaqi (person from outside) who passes the miqat and intends to enter the Haram, regardless of purpose. This includes trade, sightseeing, or any other need.
The ruling is derived from the hadith 'No one enters Makkah except with ihram.'
3
Examine the Hanafi proof: the hadith of Ibn Abbas
The Hanafi school relies on the hadith from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet said, 'No one should enter Makkah except with ihram' (لا يدخل أحد مكة إلا بإحرام). This general command indicates obligation for all.
The hadith is ahad (singular transmission), thus its thubut is zanni, but the Hanafis accept it as evidence for wujub.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i objection and the Hanafi response
Al-Shafi'i holds that ihram is only required for those intending Hajj or Umrah, citing the hadith that the Prophet entered Makkah at the conquest without ihram. The Hanafi response: that incident was specific to the Prophet and is not general for the Ummah.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that Shafi'is allow entering without ihram for non-Hajj purposes, while Hanafis require it.
5
Distinguish exceptions for those already inside the miqat or heading to the Hill
If one is a resident of the Haram area (inside the miqat), they can enter ihram from their home. If one intends to go to a place in the Hill (like Jeddah) and not the Haram, they may pass the miqat without ihram.
This shows that the obligation is tied to the intention of entering the Haram.

(ط،ع) وصح تقديمه: أي جاز الإحرام بشرط الأمن من ارتكاب محظورات الإحرام على أنه عند الأمن يكون أفضل؛ لأنه أشق فكان أعظم أجرا، وقيد بتقديمه على المواقيت؛ لأن تقديم الإحرام على أشهر الحج يكره مطلقاً، وقوله: "لا عكسه" أي لا يجوز تأخيره عن المواقيت لآفاقي قصد دخول الحرم، ولو لحاجة غير الحج كالتجارة ومجرد الرؤية أو للقتال، ودخول النبي عليه بغير إحرام يوم الفتح كان مختصا بتلك الساعة، أما لو قصد موضعا من الحل كخليص ،وجدة، حل له مجاوزة الميقات بلا إحرام فإذا حل به التحق بأهله، وقال الشافعي: لا يجب الإحرام إلا على من أراد الحج أو العمرة؛ لما روي عن جابر الله أنه عليه دخل مكة وعليه عمامة سوداء بغير إحرام، رواه مسلم والنسائي، ولنا ما روي عن ابن عباس لما أنه علي قال: "لا يدخل أحد مكة إلا بإحرام"، وما رواه كان مختصا بالنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بتلك الساعة (عيني، فتح ولداخلها : أي الميقات لداخل المواقيت في الحج والعمرة. (ط)
And the timings of ihram. Statement of the mawaqit: Dhul-Hulayfah, Dhat Irq, Juhfah, Qarn, and Yalamlam. For their people and for whoever passes by them. It is valid to perform it earlier (for the people of Madinah, for the people of Iraq, for the people of Syria, for the people of Najd). Not the opposite (i.e., it is not valid to delay beyond them). And for one inside the miqat (it is considered like the people of the Haram). The mawaqit: meaning it is not valid (to pass them without ihram). Dhul-Hulayfah: the first, with damm on the mu'jama and fatha on the lam, a place six miles from Madinah and ten stages from Makkah. The common people call it 'Abar Ali', claiming he fought jinn there, which is a lie. Dhat Irq: with kasr of the 'ayn, the place for people of Iraq. Question: How can his statement 'They are for them' apply when the people of Iraq and Syria were not Muslims? Answer: He knew by revelation of their faith, so he fixed a time for them. Juhfah: a place near Rabigh, now desolate, named because the torrent swept away its people. It is the place to which the Prophet prayed to transfer the fever of Madinah. Qarn: with fatha on qaf and sukun on ra', a mountain overlooking Arafat; opening the ra' is an error, and attributing Uways al-Qarni to it is also an error. Yalamlam: a mountain of Tihama, miqat for the people of Yemen and also for India. The mawaqit are collected in two verses: 'Irq Iraq and Yalamlam Yemen, and at Dhul-Hulayfah the Madani enters ihram, for Syria Juhfah if you pass by it, and for Najd Qarn, so understand.' So these mawaqit are for the people of these places and for whoever comes upon the miqat from other places, whether intending Hajj or Umrah or other things like trade or another need. Dhat Irq: the second, with kasr of 'ayn, for the people of Iraq, a place from which to Makkah is three days journey. Juhfah: the third, with damm on meem and sukun on ha, for the people of Syria, Egypt and the Maghreb, now called Rabigh. Qarn: the fourth, Qarn al-Manazil, also called Qarn al-Tha'alib, for people of Najd, between it and Makkah is fifty miles. Yalamlam: the fifth, with fatha on ya, lam, lam, and sukun on meem, some say Alamlam with hamza, for the people of Yemen, from it to Makkah is two farsakhs. 'For their people' means the mawaqit are for the people of those places. 'Whoever passes by them' means from those not from there who intend Hajj or Umrah. 'It is valid to perform it earlier' means it is permissible to enter ihram before the miqat, provided one is safe from committing prohibited acts of ihram, and it is better when safe because it is more arduous and thus greater reward. It is restricted to earlier than the miqat because entering ihram before the months of Hajj is generally disliked. 'Not the opposite' means it is not permissible to delay ihram beyond the miqat for an afaqi who intends to enter the Haram, even for a need other than Hajj like trade, mere sightseeing, or fighting. The Prophet's entering without ihram on the day of conquest was specific to that time. However, if one intends a place in the Hal like Khulays or Juddah, it is permissible to pass the miqat without ihram, and when he arrives there he joins its people. Al-Shafi'i said: Ihram is obligatory only on one who intends Hajj or Umrah, based on the report from Jabir that the Prophet entered Makkah with a black turban without ihram. Our proof is the report from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet said: 'No one should enter Makkah except with ihram.' And the report from Jabir was specific to the Prophet at that time. 'And for one inside it' means the miqat for one who is inside the mawaqit (for those already in the Haram area).
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling about the five fixed locations (mawaqit) for entering ihram. The author enumerates them: (1) Dhul-Hulayfah (for Madinah people), (2) Dhat Irq (for Iraq), (3) Juhfah (for Syria/Egypt/Maghreb), (4) Qarn al-Manazil (for Najd), (5) Yalamlam (for Yemen/India). Each is described with its location and distance to Makkah. The ruling: these mawaqit are for their people and for anyone passing through them who intends Hajj or Umrah, or even other purposes like trade or sightseeing. It is valid (and better when safe) to enter ihram before the miqat (i.e., earlier), but it is not valid to delay ihram beyond the miqat for an afaqi (one coming from outside) who intends to enter the Haram. An exception is if one intends a place in the Hal (like Jeddah) and not the Haram, then he can pass without ihram. The passage includes a dispute with al-Shafi'i, who holds that ihram is required only for Hajj or Umrah, not for other purposes. The Hanafi proof is the hadith from Ibn Abbas that no one should enter Makkah except with ihram, and the incident of the Prophet's entry without ihram at the conquest is specific to him. The passage also notes that for those already inside the miqat (i.e., residents of Makkah or the Haram area), their miqat is the place where they reside (they can enter ihram from their homes).

Key Terms
ميقات (miqat): A fixed location or time for entering ihram; here it refers to the five designated places.
الآفاقي (al-afaqi): One who comes from outside the mawaqit (i.e., from beyond the boundaries).
الحل (al-hill): The area outside the Haram boundary but inside the miqat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Wait outside Makkah

Key Takeaway
The five mawaqit are fixed locations where ihram becomes wajib for anyone entering the Haram, regardless of purpose, based on the general command of the Prophet.

Mawaaqit and Rulings for the Afaqi
Explaining the five miqat boundaries and obligations for outsiders

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the obligation of ihram for an afaqi entering Makkah and distinguish the Hanafi proof from the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Ihram at the miqat is wajib for every afaqi entering Makkah, even for trade or sightseeing.

In the previous lesson, we learned the locations of the five mawaaqit. This passage builds on that by explaining the legal ruling: who is obligated to enter ihram at these boundaries? The Hanafi position, grounded in the hadith of Ibn Abbas, extends the obligation to all afaqis entering Makkah, including for non-ritual purposes. A key dispute with the Shafi'i school hinges on the interpretation of the Prophet's own entry without ihram during the Conquest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is entering Makkah as an afaqi (someone from outside the miqat area). The ruling is that it is wajib to enter with ihram.
This obligation applies even if the purpose is not Hajj or Umrah.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas (marfu): 'لا يدخل أحد مكة إلا بإحرام' — 'No one should enter Makkah except with ihram.'
This is a hadith ahad, but it is accepted as evidence for wujub in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith uses a negative command (nahi) with an exception. In Hanafi usul, a nahi indicates prohibition, and the exception 'except with ihram' makes it obligatory to enter with ihram. The ruling is derived from the principle that al-amr wa al-nahy yufid al-wujub.
This is a zanni dalalah, but strong enough for wujub.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that ihram is only required for those intending Hajj or Umrah, based on the hadith of Jabir that the Prophet entered Makkah without ihram at the Conquest.
Shafi'i considers the Ibn Abbas hadith as general but overridden by the specific act of the Prophet.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi response is that the Prophet's entry without ihram was specific to that occasion (the Conquest) and does not abrogate the general command. The general ruling from Ibn Abbas remains.
The mufta bihi is the Hanafi position: ihram is wajib for any afaqi entering Makkah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج بيان المواقيت ذو الحليفة وذات عرق وجحفة وقرن ويلملم لأهلها ولمن مرّ بها، وصح تقديمه لأهل المدينة لأهل العراق لأهل الشام لأهل نجد عليها، لا عكسه، ولداخلها الحل، المواقيت أي لا يصح ذو الحليفة: أي الأول، بضم المهملة وفتح اللام مكان على ستة أميال من المدينة، وعشر مراحل من مكة، تسميها العوام آبار علي، يزعمون أنه قاتل الجن في بعضها وهو كذب، و"ذات عرق" بالكسر قلت: كيف يتأتى قوله علي: "هن لهن وأهل العراق والشام لم يكونوا مسلمين؟ أجيب بأنه عليها علم بطريق الوحي إيمانهم فوقت لهم، و"جحفة" موضع بالقرب من رابغ، وهي رسم خال لا يسكن به، سميت بذلك؛ لأن السيل جحف أهلها أي استأصلهم وهي التي دعا النبي عليه أن تنقل إليها حمى المدينة، و"قرن" بفتح القاف وسكون الراء جبل مطل على عرفات وفتح الراء فيه خطأ، ونسبة أويس الله إليه خطأ، آخر وجه التخطئة أن المتحرك اسم قبيلة ينسب إليها أويس القرني، و"يلملم" هو جبل من جبل تهامة ميقات أهل اليمن وهو ميقات أهل الهند أيضاً، والمواقيت جمعت في بيتين: عرق العراق ويلملم اليمن وبذي الحليفة يحرم المدني للشام جحفة إن مررت بها ولأهل نجد قرن فاستبن فهذه المواقيت لأهل هذه الأمكنة ولمن أتى على الميقات من غير أهلها ممن أراد الحج والعمرة أو غيرهما كتجارة أو حاجة أخرى. (فتح) وذات عرق أي الثاني بكسر العين لأهل العراق موضع منه إلى مكة مسيرة ثلاثة أيام. (عيني) وجحفة: أي الثالث، بضم الميم وسكون الهاء المهملة لأهل الشام ومصر ومغرب وهو المسمى الآن بـ"رابغ". (ط،ع) وقرن: أي الرابع قرن المنازل، ويقال له: قرن الثعالب لأهل نجد بينه وبين مكة خمسون ميلا (ط، ع) ويلملم: أي الخامس يلملم بفتح التحتية واللامين وسكون الميم بينهما، وقيل: ألملم بالهمزة لأهل اليمن منه إلى مكة فرسخان. (ط،ع) لأهلها: أي المواقيت تكون لأهل هذه الأمكنة. (مسكين مر بها أي بهذه المواضع من غير أهلها ممن أراد الحج أو العمرة. (ط،ع) وصح تقديمه: أي جاز الإحرام بشرط الأمن من ارتكاب محظورات الإحرام على أنه عند الأمن يكون أفضل؛ لأنه أشق فكان أعظم أجرا، وقيد بتقديمه على المواقيت؛ لأن تقديم الإحرام على أشهر الحج يكره مطلقاً، وقوله: "لا عكسه" أي لا يجوز تأخيره عن المواقيت لآفاقي قصد دخول الحرم، ولو لحاجة غير الحج كالتجارة ومجرد الرؤية أو للقتال، ودخول النبي عليه بغير إحرام يوم الفتح كان مختصا بتلك الساعة، أما لو قصد موضعا من الحل كخليص وجدة، حل له مجاوزة الميقات بلا إحرام فإذا حل به التحق بأهله، وقال الشافعي: لا يجب الإحرام إلا على من أراد الحج أو العمرة؛ لما روي عن جابر الله أنه عليه دخل مكة وعليه عمامة سوداء بغير إحرام، رواه مسلم والنسائي، ولنا ما روي عن ابن عباس لما أنه علي قال: "لا يدخل أحد مكة إلا بإحرام"، وما رواه كان مختصا بالنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بتلك الساعة (عيني، فتح ولداخلها : أي الميقات لداخل المواقيت في الحج والعمرة. (ط)
The Book of Hajj. Explanation of the Miqats: Dhul-Hulayfah, Dhat 'Irq, Juhfah, Qarn, and Yalamlam. They are for their people and for whoever passes by them. It is valid to advance the ihram for the people of Madinah, for the people of Iraq, for the people of Sham, and for the people of Najd over them, not the reverse. And for those inside the miqat, the Hill [is the miqat]. The miqat: meaning it is not valid... Dhul-Hulayfah: the first, with damm of the important letter and fat-ha of the lam, a place six miles from Madinah and ten stages from Makkah. The common people call it 'Well of Ali', claiming he fought the jinn in some of them, which is a lie. And 'Dhat 'Irq' with kasr: I said: How does his saying: 'they are for them' come about when the people of Iraq and Sham were not Muslims? The answer: He knew by way of revelation of their faith, so he set a miqat for them. And 'Juhfah': a place near Rabigh, a ruin with no inhabitants, so named because the flood carried away its people. It is the one the Prophet prayed to transfer the fever of Madinah to. And 'Qarn' with fat-h of the qaf and sukun of the ra: a mountain overlooking Arafat; opening the ra is a mistake, and attributing Uways al-Qarni to it is a mistake. Another face of correction: that the moving [letter] is a tribe name to which Uways al-Qarni is attributed. And 'Yalamlam' is a mountain in Tihamah, the miqat of the people of Yemen, and also the miqat of the people of India. The miqats are summarized in two verses: 'Iraq's 'Irq and Yemen's Yalamlam, and at Dhul-Hulayfah the Madani enters ihram; for Sham, Juhfah if you pass by it, and for the people of Najd, Qarn, so understand.' So these miqats are for the people of these places and for whoever comes upon the miqat from other than its people intending Hajj/Umrah or other things like trade or another need. (Fath) And 'Dhat 'Irq': the second, with kasr of the 'ayn, for the people of Iraq, a place from which to Makkah is a journey of three days. ('Ayni) And 'Juhfah': the third, with damm of the mim and sukun of the ha, for the people of Sham, Egypt, and Maghrib, and it is now called 'Rabigh'. (T, 'A) And 'Qarn': the fourth, Qarn al-Manazil, also called Qarn al-Tha'alib, for the people of Najd, distance from Makkah fifty miles. (T, 'A) And 'Yalamlam': the fifth, Yalamlam with fat-h of the ya and the two lams and sukun of the mim between them, some say Alamlum with hamzah, for the people of Yemen, from it to Makkah two parasangs. (T, 'A) 'For its people': meaning the miqats are for the people of these places. (Miskin) 'Whoever passes by them': meaning by these places from other than its people who intends Hajj or Umrah. (T, 'A) 'And it is valid to advance it': meaning ihram is permitted with the condition of safety from committing prohibitions of ihram, but when safe it is better because it is more difficult and thus greater reward, and it is restricted to advancing before the miqat because advancing ihram before the months of Hajj is detested absolutely. And his saying: 'not the reverse' means it is not permissible to delay it beyond the miqat for an afaqi who intends to enter the Haram, even for a need other than Hajj, like trade, mere sightseeing, or fighting. The Prophet's entry without ihram on the day of Conquest was specific to that moment. But if he intends a place in the Hill like Khulays or Jeddah, it is permissible for him to pass the miqat without ihram, and when he arrives there he joins its people. Al-Shafi'i said: Ihram is obligatory only on one who intends Hajj or Umrah, due to the narration from Jabir that the Prophet entered Makkah with a black turban without ihram, reported by Muslim and Nasa'i. Our proof is what is narrated from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet said: 'No one should enter Makkah except with ihram.' And his narration was specific to the Prophet at that time. ('Ayni, Fath) And 'for those inside it': meaning the miqat for those inside the miqats in Hajj and Umrah. (T)
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the mawaaqit (fixed places for ihram) from the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq. The author begins by listing the five miqats: Dhul-Hulayfah for the people of Madinah, Dhat 'Irq for Iraq, Juhfah for Sham, Qarn for Najd, and Yalamlam for Yemen. He notes that these are also for anyone passing through them intending Hajj, Umrah, or even other purposes like trade. The text then discusses advancing ihram before the miqat: it is permissible and even recommended when safe, as it increases difficulty and reward. However, delaying ihram past the miqat is not allowed for an afaqi (someone from outside the Haram area) under any circumstances, including for non-ritual purposes. The exception is the Prophet's entry without ihram at the Conquest of Makkah, which was specific. A Shafi'i objection is addressed: Al-Shafi'i argued that ihram is only required for those intending Hajj/Umrah, citing the hadith of Jabir. The Hanafi response cites the hadith of Ibn Abbas ('No one should enter Makkah except with ihram') and argues the Prophet's case was unique. The passage concludes with the miqat for those already inside the miqat area: they must enter ihram from their place (the Hill) for Umrah, and from the Haram for Hajj, as detailed in the next lesson.

Key Terms
الميقات (al-miqat): The fixed boundary place where a pilgrim must enter the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah.
أفقي (afaqi): A person who lives outside the miqat area (i.e., beyond the five mawaaqit), as opposed to a resident of the Haram or the miqat areas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for an afaqi who passes the miqat without ihram intending only trade in Makkah?
A) He may enter Makkah without ihram because he did not intend Hajj/Umrah.
B) He must enter ihram before the miqat; otherwise he must return to the miqat or sacrifice.
C) He can enter Makkah without ihram if he is a merchant.
D) He should enter Makkah without ihram and then perform Umrah.

Key Takeaway
Ihram at the miqat is wajib for every afaqi entering Makkah, regardless of purpose, based on the general command of the Prophet (PBUH), with the exception of the Prophet's own entry at the Conquest.

Miqat for Residents of the Haram: Hajj and Umrah
Defining miqat for Haram residents with proof and wisdom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the miqat ruling for residents of the Haram for both Hajj and Umrah, and explain the proof (dalil) and wisdom behind it.

Core Idea
For a Makkan: Hajj ihram from the Haram; Umrah ihram from the Hill—to create a journey.

While Muslims from around the world travel to designated miqats on the borders of the Haram, those already living inside the sacred precincts have a different rule. They can begin their Hajj ihram from anywhere within the Haram, but for Umrah they must exit the Haram to the Hill (al-Ḥill). This lesson clarifies the ruling, its proof, the preferred location (al-Tan‘im), and the wisdom behind this distinction.

Guided Path
1
State the two rulings
From the text: 'Wal-makki al-haram lil-hajj wal-hill lil-‘umrah.' Identify the miqat for each act.
2
Examine the proof
The author cites the Prophet's practice: 'kaan ya'mur bi-dhalika.' In Hanafi usul, a command from the Prophet indicates obligation (wujub) unless diverted.
Dalil type: Sunnah ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Understand the wisdom (ḥikma)
To achieve a type of travel: for Hajj (performed at ‘Arafat in the Hill), ihram from the Haram creates a journey from Haram to Hill; for Umrah (performed in the Haram), ihram from the Hill creates a journey from Hill to Haram.
4
Note the preferred place for Umrah
The text says 'al-Tan‘im afḍal' - al-Tan‘im near Masjid ‘A’ishah is the best place for a Makkan to enter ihram for Umrah.
Other parts of the Hill are also valid.
5
Recognize the boundaries of the Haram
The text provides distances: from Madinah 3 miles, from Yemen/Iraq/Ta’if 7 miles, from Jeddah 10 miles, from Ji‘ranah 9 miles. These define who is a ‘resident of the Haram’.
Cross-madhhab: boundaries are agreed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللمكي الحرم للحج والحل للعمرة. أي الميقات لساكن مكة ويلحق به القارني حرمها وإن لم يكن مكياً، والمراد به من كان داخل الحرم سواء كان بمكة أو لا، والحرم حوالي مكة، وقد نظم حدود الحرم في بيتين: وللحرم التحديد من أرض طيبة ثلاثة أميال إذا رمت اتقانه ومن يمن سبع عراق وطائف وجدة عشر ثم تسع جعرانة الحرم حد الحرم من طريق المدينة ثلاثة أميال ومن طريق اليمن والعراق والطائف سبعة، ومن طريق جدة عشرة، ومن الجعرانة تسعة. (ط) والحل للعمرة أي ميقات المكي الحل للعمرة ليتحقق نوع سفر، والتنعيم أفضل، وهو موضع بقرب مكة عند مسجد عائشة ما أي ميقات المكي إذا أراد العمرة الحل والعمرة اسم من الاعتمار، وأصله القصد إلى مكان عامر ثم غلب استعماله في زيارة البيت محرما بأفعال مخصوصة، وإنما سميت بها؛ لأن عمارة البيت بها، وإنما كان ميقات المكي لمريد الحج الحرم ولمريد العمرة الحل؛ لأنه علي كان يأمر بذلك؛ ولأن أداء الحج في عرفة وهي في الحل، فيكون الإحرام من الحرم؛ ليتحقق نوع سفر، وأداء العمرة في الحرم فيكون الإحرام من الحل؛ ليتحقق نوع سفر بتبديل المكان، وسبب تحريم الحرم قال بعض أهل العلم لما خاف آدم عليه على نفسه من الشيطان استعاذ بالله فأرسل ملائكة حفوا بمكة من كل جانب ووقفوا حواليها فحرم الله الحرم من حيث كانت الملائكة وقفت. (مسكين، فتح)
And for the Makkan: the Haram is for Hajj, and the Hill is for Umrah. That is the miqat for the resident of Makkah. The qarin (one who combines Hajj and Umrah) of the Haram is included even if not a Makkan. What is meant is whoever is inside the Haram, whether in Makkah or not. The Haram is around Makkah. The boundaries of the Haram have been organized in two verses: 'For the Haram, the limit from the land of Taybah is three miles if you intend its perfection; from Yemen, seven; Iraq, Ta'if, and Jeddah ten; then from Ji'ranah nine.' The limit of the Haram from the road of Madinah is three miles, from the road of Yemen, Iraq, and Ta'if seven, from the road of Jeddah ten, and from Ji'ranah nine. (T) And the Hill for Umrah: meaning the miqat of the Makkan is the Hill for Umrah to achieve a type of travel. The best is al-Tan'im, a place near Makkah at the mosque of Aisha. That is the miqat of the Makkan when he intends Umrah: the Hill. Umrah is derived from i'timar, originally meaning intending an inhabited place, then used for visiting the House in ihram with specific actions. It is so named because the House is inhabited by it. And indeed the miqat of the Makkan for the one desiring Hajj is the Haram, and for the one desiring Umrah is the Hill, because the Prophet used to command that, and because Hajj is performed at Arafat which is in the Hill, so ihram from the Haram achieves a type of travel, and Umrah is performed in the Haram so ihram from the Hill achieves a type of travel by changing location. The cause of the sanctity of the Haram: Some scholars said that when Adam feared for himself from the Shaytan, he sought refuge in Allah, so Allah sent angels who surrounded Makkah from every side and stood around it, so Allah sanctified the Haram from where the angels stood. (Miskin, Fath)
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage completes the discussion of miqats by addressing those who reside within the Haram, i.e., the people of Makkah and anyone living inside the Haram boundaries. The author states the ruling: for Hajj, their miqat is the Haram itself; they can enter ihram from their homes or any place within the Haram. For Umrah, their miqat is the Hill (al-Hall), the area outside the Haram. The best place for Umrah ihram is al-Tan'im (near Masjid Aisha). The wisdom behind this is to ensure that the worshipper experiences a type of travel: for Hajj, the main rite (Arafat) is in the Hill, so ihram from the Haram creates a journey from Haram to Hill; for Umrah, the main rite (tawaf) is in the Haram, so ihram from the Hill creates a journey from Hill to Haram. The passage then gives the precise boundaries of the Haram in verses and mentions a report on the origin of its sanctity related to Prophet Adam. This establishes the ruling with both textual evidence (the Prophet's command) and rational wisdom.

Key Terms
الحل (al-hill): The area outside the Haram boundaries, i.e., the non-sanctified territory around Makkah, which is the miqat for Umrah for residents of the Haram.
الحرم (al-haram): The sacred territory around Makkah with defined boundaries, within which certain acts are restricted; it is the miqat for Hajj for its residents.
التنعيم (al-tan'im): A place near Makkah, specifically at the Mosque of Aisha, considered the best miqat for Umrah for a Makkan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Where must a resident of Makkah enter ihram for Umrah according to the Hanafi school?
A) From any place within the Haram.
B) From the Hill (outside the Haram), preferably al-Tan'im.
C) From the miqat of his home city.
D) He does not need to enter ihram for Umrah.

Key Takeaway
A resident of the Haram must enter ihram for Hajj from within the Haram and for Umrah from the Hill, because the Prophet commanded it and to achieve a meaningful journey.

Miqat for the Resident of Makkah (Makki)
Explains miqat for Makki for Hajj and Umrah with proof from Ali's practice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the miqat for a Makki for Hajj and Umrah and explain the Hanafi proof from the practice of Ali.

Core Idea
A Makki enters ihram for Hajj from the Haram and for Umrah from the Hill to ensure a journey.

This lesson clarifies the unique miqat rules for those residing in Makkah or within the Haram. Unlike outsiders who enter from designated miqats, the Makki has different starting points for Hajj and Umrah. The ruling is based on the practice of Ali ibn Abi Talib and the logical requirement of undertaking a journey for each rite.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
The 'Makki' refers to anyone residing in Makkah or within the Haram boundaries, not necessarily a native of Makkah. The passage clarifies that this includes the qarin (one performing Hajj and Umrah together) who is within the Haram.
2
State the ruling
For Hajj, the miqat is the Haram itself; for Umrah, the miqat is the Hill (the area outside the Haram). This is the core ruling presented in the matn.
3
Understand the proof
The passage cites the practice of Ali ibn Abi Talib (رضي الله عنه) as the evidence. In the Hanafi school, the practice of a Companion can serve as a source of legislation (qawl sahabi).
The wisdom behind the rule is to ensure a type of journey: for Hajj, one travels from Haram to Arafat (in the Hill); for Umrah, one travels from Hill to Haram.
4
Appreciate the expansion
The commentary provides precise boundaries of the Haram, but the essential fiqh point remains the distinction between Hajj and Umrah miqat for the Makki. The historical narration about Adam adds context but is not part of the legal ruling.

كتاب الحج
بيان المواقيت
وللمكي الحرم للحج والحل للعمرة.
أي الميقات لساكن مكة
وللمكي إلخ: يعني ساكن مكة ويلحق به القارني حرمها وإن لم يكن مكياً، والمراد به من كان داخل الحرم سواء كان بمكة أو لا، والحرم حوالي مكة، وقد نظم حدود الحرم في بيتين:
وللحرم التحديد من أرض طيبة ثلاثة أميال إذا رمت
اتقانه
ومن يمن سبع عراق وطائف وجدة عشر ثم تسع جعرانة
الحرم حد الحرم من طريق المدينة ثلاثة أميال ومن طريق اليمن والعراق والطائف سبعة، ومن طريق جدة عشرة، ومن الجعرانة تسعة. (ط)
والحل للعمرة [ أي ميقات المكي الحل للعمرة ليتحقق نوع سفر، والتنعيم أفضل، وهو موضع بقرب مكة عند مسجد عائشة ما] أي ميقات المكي إذا أراد العمرة الحل والعمرة اسم من الاعتمار، وأصله القصد إلى مكان عامر ثم غلب استعماله في زيارة البيت محرما بأفعال مخصوصة، وإنما سميت بها؛ لأن عمارة البيت بها، وإنما كان ميقات المكي لمريد الحج الحرم ولمريد العمرة الحل؛ لأنه علي كان يأمر بذلك؛ ولأن أداء الحج في عرفة وهي في الحل، فيكون الإحرام من الحرم؛ ليتحقق نوع سفر، وأداء العمرة في الحرم فيكون الإحرام من الحل؛ ليتحقق نوع سفر بتبديل المكان، وسبب تحريم الحرم قال بعض أهل العلم لما خاف آدم عليه على نفسه من الشيطان استعاذ بالله فأرسل ملائكة حفوا بمكة من كل جانب ووقفوا حواليها فحرم الله الحرم من حيث كانت الملائكة وقفت. (مسكين، فتح)
Book of Hajj. Statement of the Miqat. For the Makki, the Haram is for Hajj and the Hill is for Umrah. i.e. the miqat for the resident of Makkah. 'And for the Makki etc.' means: the resident of Makkah, and joined to him is the one in the Haram even if not a Makki, and what is meant is whoever is inside the Haram whether in Makkah or not, and the Haram surrounds Makkah. The boundaries of the Haram have been organized in two lines: For the Haram, the boundary from the land of Tayyibah is three miles if you intend its precision, and from Yemen seven, from Iraq and Ta'if seven, from Jeddah ten, then from Ji'ranah nine. The Haram boundary from the Madinah road is three miles, from the Yemen, Iraq and Ta'if roads seven, from the Jeddah road ten, and from Ji'ranah nine. And the Hill is for Umrah [i.e. the miqat of the Makki for Umrah is the Hill to realize a type of journey, and al-Tan'im is best, which is a place near Makkah at the mosque of Aisha what] i.e. the miqat of the Makki when he intends Umrah is the Hill, and Umrah is a name from i'timar, originally meaning intention to an inhabited place, then its usage prevailed for visiting the House in ihram with specific actions, and it is named so because the House is inhabited through it. The miqat of the Makki for one desiring Hajj is the Haram, and for one desiring Umrah is the Hill, because Ali used to command that, and because performing Hajj is at Arafat which is in the Hill, so ihram is from the Haram to realize a type of journey, and performing Umrah is in the Haram, so ihram is from the Hill to realize a type of journey by changing place. The reason the Haram was made sacred: some scholars said that when Adam feared for himself from Satan, he sought refuge in Allah, so Allah sent angels who surrounded Makka from every side and stood around it, so Allah made the Haram sacred from where the angels stood.

Commentary
This passage explains the miqat (boundary for entering ihram) for a person residing in Makkah or within the Haram. The ruling is that such a person enters ihram for Hajj from the Haram itself, and for Umrah from the Hill (the area outside the Haram). The commentary expands on the boundaries of the Haram, giving precise distances from various directions. The reason for this distinction is to ensure a journey: for Hajj, one begins from the Haram and travels to Arafat (in the Hill); for Umrah, one begins from the Hill and enters the Haram. This is based on the practice of Ali ibn Abi Talib. The passage also includes a narration about the origin of the Haram's sanctity from the time of Adam.

Key Terms
ميقات (miqat): The designated boundary (spatial or temporal) for entering into ihram for Hajj or Umrah.
حرم (haram): The sacred precinct around Makkah within which certain acts are forbidden.
حل (hill): The area outside the Haram, which serves as the miqat for Umrah for residents of Makkah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
For a person residing in Makkah who intends to perform Hajj, what is his miqat?
A) The Hill (al-Hall)
B) The Haram (al-Haram)
C) The same as for others
D) The miqat of Dhu al-Hulayfah

Key Takeaway
A Makki's miqat for Hajj is the Haram, and for Umrah is the Hill, based on the practice of Ali.

Recommended Acts Before Ihram: Wudu, Ghusl, and Clothing
Describes sunan of ihram: wudu, ghusl, and clothing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah acts performed before entering ihram (wudu/ghusl and clothing) and explain the preference for ghusl based on the prophetic hadith.

Core Idea
Before ihram, perform ghusl or wudu; ghusl is more virtuous, and wear unstitched izar and rida — these are sunnah, not fard.

This passage from the Kanz al-Daqa'iq commentary introduces the recommended practices for someone about to enter the state of ihram. The author clarifies that both wudu and ghusl are acceptable, but ghusl is superior, as evidenced by the Prophet's own practice. It also details the proper attire: two unstitched garments (izar and rida), with a preference for new or clean white cloths. Understanding these sunan helps a pilgrim fulfill the ihram with optimal merit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage covers two categories of recommended acts: purification (wudu/ghusl) and clothing (izar and rida). Recognize that both are sunnah muakkadah, not fard.
The text explicitly says 'والغسل أحب' (ghusl is more beloved), indicating preference.
2
Locate the dalil for ghusl
The author cites the hadith of Zayd ibn Thabit that the Prophet performed ghusl for his ihram. This hadith is the proof for recommending ghusl.
Hadith narrated by al-Tirmidhi and deemed hasan.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action of performing ghusl specifically for ihram indicates that it is a recommended act. The Hanafi school uses this as evidence for sunnah.
The purpose is cleanliness, not ritual purification; hence menstruating women are also commanded to do it.
4
Analyze the clothing requirements
The sunnah is to wear an izar (lower wrap) and a rida (upper wrap), both unstitched. New or washed white garments are preferred. If only the izar is worn, it suffices for covering the awrah.
The izar covers from navel to knee, the rida covers the upper body.
5
Note additional recommended actions
The passage also recommends trimming nails, shaving pubic hair, plucking armpit hair, and washing the body with cleansers. These enhance cleanliness before ihram.
These are not obligatory but complement the sunnah.

It is linguistically a verbal noun of 'ahrama' meaning entered into an inviolable sanctity. Covering the awrah and repelling heat and cold are necessary, and these two garments fulfill that. The new ones are better because they are closer to purity; if not found, then washed ones because they resemble new in that sense. Wearing both is sunnah; if one restricts to the izar alone, it suffices due to covering the awrah. Commentary
This passage begins the chapter on ihram, defining it linguistically and legally. It explains that ihram is realized through intention and talbiyah (or a specific act), and is a fard of Hajj like standing at Arafat. The focus then shifts to recommended acts before entering ihram. The text states: 'When you intend to enter ihram, perform wudu, and ghusl is more beloved.' The commentary clarifies that the sunnah is to have one of the two purifications, with ghusl being superior due to a hadith of Zayd ibn Thabit that the Prophet performed ghusl for ihram. This ghusl is for cleanliness, not ritual purity, so even menstruating women are commanded to do it. It is also recommended to thoroughly clean the body. For clothing, the sunnah is to wear an izar (lower garment) and rida (upper garment), both unstitched. New garments are preferred, then washed. If only the izar is worn, it is sufficient for covering the awrah.

Key Terms
إحرام (ihram): The state of consecration for Hajj or Umrah, entered by intention and talbiyah/specific act, prohibiting certain actions.
غسل (ghusl): Full-body wash; here it is a sunnah act for cleanliness before ihram, not for ritual purification.
إزار (izar): A waist-wrapper covering from navel to knees, worn by men in ihram.
رداء (rida): A cloak worn over the shoulders, covering the upper body, unstitched.

Definition and Preparatory Acts of Ihram
Definition and recommended preparatory acts for Ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of ihram, identify its two conditions, and list the recommended preparatory acts including ghusl and attire.

Core Idea
Ihram requires both intention and a verbal/act initiation; its ghusl is for cleanliness, not ritual purity.

This lesson introduces the chapter on Ihram, the sacred state for Hajj and Umrah. We will unpack the classical definition, distinguishing the essential conditions from the highly recommended acts. Understanding this foundation is crucial for performing the rites correctly according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Define Ihram linguistically and legally
Extract the linguistic meaning (entering sanctity) and the legal meaning (commitment to specific prohibitions). Note that the legal realization requires two elements: intention (niyyah) plus either verbal mention (dhikr) or a specific act (like wearing the two garments).
Hanafi: intention alone is insufficient without a accompanying action.
2
Identify the obligatory status of Ihram
Recognize that ihram is a fard (obligatory pillar) of Hajj, compared to the takbir of iftitah in prayer. It is not merely a recommended act.
3
Analyze the recommended purifications: wudu vs ghusl
Note that both wudu and ghusl are sunnah, but ghusl is more virtuous. Understand that this ghusl is for cleanliness, not ritual purity, so it applies even to menstruating women. The virtue is only attained if one maintains wudu after ghusl.
Tayammum is not substituted for this ghusl, unlike for Friday and Eid.
4
List other recommended acts of grooming and preparation
Identify the additional sunan: trimming nails, removing hair (armpit, pubic), marital relations, shaving head (if accustomed), combing hair, washing with cleansing agents.
These are for cleanliness and comfort during ihram.
5
Specify the attire for Ihram
The recommended garments are an unsewn izar (lower) and rida (upper). New is best, then washed. Wearing both is sunnah, but the izar alone suffices if it covers the awrah. The prohibition of sewn garments is derived from the Prophet's practice.

Chapter of Ihram [i.e., regarding its rulings and modality. (Ayni) When the author mentioned the mawaqit which it is not permissible for a person to exceed except in the state of ihram, it was appropriate to mention ihram. It is linguistically a masdar of 'ahrama' meaning 'he entered into an inviolable sanctity'. Legally: entering into specific prohibitions – i.e., committing to them – but it is not legally realized except with intention along with verbal mention or specific act, so both are conditions for the realization of ihram. Thus ihram for hajj is like the takbir of iftitah for prayer. It is called ihram because it renders permissible things forbidden. (Fath, Mustakhlas) 'Perform wudu: if you wish, otherwise perform ghusl. And ghusl is more beloved': meaning that the sunnah for ihram is one of the two purifications, with a difference in virtue between them. So ghusl is better due to what is related from Zayd ibn Thabit that he (the Prophet) performed ghusl for his ihram, narrated by al-Tirmidhi and he deemed it hasan, because it is more general and more effective in cleansing. The intent of this ghusl is to obtain cleanliness and remove foul odor, not ritual purity, so the menstruating woman and postpartum woman are commanded to do it. It is related that he (the Prophet) commanded Abu Bakr (when his wife Asma gave birth) to tell her to perform ghusl and enter ihram for hajj, even though ritual purity is not conceivable for her. Hence tayammum is not considered when unable to find water, unlike Friday and Eid.

So if he breaks his wudu, then performs wudu and enters ihram, he does not attain its virtue, because it is legislated for ihram. Also recommended are complete cleansing: trimming nails, plucking armpit hair, shaving pubic hair, marital relations, shaving the head for one accustomed, combing hair for one not accustomed, and washing the body with mallow and kali etc. (Ayni, Mustakhlas, Fath) 'Izar': the izar is what is from the navel to the knee. (Mustakhlas) 'Rida': the rida is what is on the back from the shoulders. (Mustakhlas) 'An izar and rida': the izar is from the waist, the rida is from the shoulders, and they must be unsewn, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) wore the izar and rida when he entered ihram, and because he is prohibited from wearing sewn garments. It is necessary to cover the private parts and to repel heat and cold, and that is in what we specified. Then new is better because it is closer to purity; if not found, then washed, because it resembles it in this meaning. Then wearing both together is a sunnah, so if he limits himself to the izar, it suffices him due to covering the private parts. (Mustakhlas, Fath)
'New': meaning they are in a state of newness because it is cleaner and farther from dirt. (Ayni)
'Washed': meaning if you do not find new ones, and it is better that they be white. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on Ihram by defining the term and laying out the recommended acts for entering the sacred state. The commentator first gives the definition: linguistically, ihram means entering into sanctity; legally, it is the commitment to specific prohibitions, which is only realized through intention (niyyah) combined with either verbal mention (talbiyah or other dhikr) or a specific act (like wearing the two garments). These two—intention and speech/act—are conditions (shartan) for the validity of ihram. The author analogizes ihram in hajj to the opening takbir in salah: both require intention and an initiating action. Ihram is a fard (obligatory pillar) of hajj, on par with standing at Arafah and Tawaf al-Ziyarah.

The author then addresses the student directly, encouraging study of ihram's rulings. Some narrations indicate Abu Hanifah addressed Abu Yusuf, or that the author wrote for his son. The recommended acts (sunnah) before ihram are: (1) wudu, but ghusl is superior because the Prophet performed ghusl for entering ihram. This ghusl is for cleanliness, not ritual purity, so menstruating and postpartum women are also commanded to do it, though they cannot attain ritual purity. Therefore, tayammum is not substituted when water is absent, unlike ghusl for Friday and Eid. To earn the sunnah, one must be in the state of wudu from the ghusl; if one breaks wudu after ghusl and then does wudu before ihram, the virtue is lost. Additional recommended grooming includes trimming nails, armpit and pubic hair, marital intercourse before ihram, shaving the head for those accustomed, combing hair, and washing with cleansing agents.

For garments, the recommended set is an izar (lower garment from navel to knee) and a rida (upper wrap from shoulders), both unsewn. This follows the Prophet's practice and avoids prohibited sewn clothing. New garments are best for purity; if unavailable, washed ones suffice. Wearing both is sunnah, but the izar alone suffices if it covers the awrah.

Key Terms
الإحرام (al-ihrami): Legally: entering into specific prohibitions (hurmah) for hajj/umrah, realized by intention and utterance or specific act.
الغسل (al-ghusl): Washing the entire body; recommended for ihram for cleanliness, not ritual purity.
الإزار (al-izar): Lower garment from navel to knee, unsewn.
الرداء (al-rida): Upper garment covering shoulders and back, unsewn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi commentary, what is the ruling if a person enters ihram only with intention and without any verbal mention or specific act?
A) The ihram is valid because intention is the essence.
B) The ihram is not valid; it requires either dhikr or a specific act.
C) The ihram is valid but makruh.
D) The ihram is valid only if he wears the two garments.

Key Takeaway
Ihram in the Hanafi school requires both intention (niyyah) and an accompanying outward element (dhikr or specific act) to be valid; the ghusl before ihram is for cleanliness and not a substitute for minor purity.
