The Hanafi Ruling on Applying Perfume before Ihram
Ruling on applying perfume before ihram and rebuttal of opposing views

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on applying perfume before ihram, identify the supporting dalil, and explain the rebuttal to the opposing view using the concept of naskh.

Core Idea
Perfume before ihram is sunnah; lingering residue does not violate the prohibition because it was applied before the state.

You may have heard that perfume is forbidden during ihram. But what about applying it before entering the state? This lesson examines the Hanafi position that it is not only allowed but recommended, based on the Prophet's own practice, and addresses the objection that any trace should be removed. We will also explore an intra-Hanafi difference and the cross-madhhab dispute with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The act is applying perfume to the body (not the garment) before entering ihram. The author states it is sunnah (recommended) with any perfume.
The phrase 'على وجه السنة' indicates the ruling level.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the evidence cited. The author gives the hadith of Aishah (ra) that she perfumed the Prophet for his ihram with the best perfume, narrated by Bukhari and Muslim.
This is a dalil from authentic sunnah (ahad, but qati al-thubut due to Bukhari/Muslim).
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Muhammad and Zufar (two Hanafi imams) considered it disliked (makruh tanzih) if the perfume leaves a visible residue after ihram, because sweat might transfer it to another spot, resembling new application.
This is an internal disagreement within the Hanafi school.
4
Analyze the opposing view and its dalil
Imam al-Shafi'i agrees with Muhammad and Zufar, citing a hadith where the Prophet commanded a man in ihram to wash off perfume three times. The Hanafi response rebuts this evidence.
The Shafi'i ruling is that any perfume trace must be removed before or right after ihram.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school responds with stronger evidence: additional reports from Aishah showing the Prophet's glistening perfume after ihram, and the fact that women applied musk and he did not forbid. The opposing hadith is deemed abrogated (mansukh) because it was from the Year of Conquest (umrah), while the Hanafi evidence is from the Farewell Pilgrimage (hajj). Also, the prohibition only applies to new application after ihram, not to residual trace.
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the view of Abu Hanifah: sunnah and residue permissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتطيب [ أي طيب بدنك إن وجدت لا ثوبك بما تبقى عينه. (ط)] على وجه السنة بأي طيب شئت؛ لما ورد عن عائشة ما أنها قالت: "كنت أطيب رسول الله له بأطيب ما أجد"، رواه البخاري ومسلم، وكره محمد وزفر بما تبقى عينه بعد الإحرام؛ لأنه إذا عرق ينتقل إلى محل آخر من بدنه، فيكون بمنزلة ابتداء التطيب، و به قال الشافعي أيضاً؛ لقوله عليها الرجل محرم سأله عما كان عليه من الطيب: "أما الطيب الذي بك فاغسله ثلاث مرات"، ولنا : ما ورد عن عائشة لها أنه علي كان إذا أراد أن يحرم يتطيب بأطيب ما يجد، ثم أرى وبيص الطيب، وفي رواية: وبيص الدهن في رأسه ولحيته، وعنها أيضاً أنها قالت: كنا نخرج . معه علينا إلى مكة فنضمد جباهنا بالمسك المطيب عند الإحرام، فإذا عرقت إحدانا سال على وجهها فيراه عليه، ولا ينهانا عنه، وما رواه منسوخ؛ لأنه كان في عام الفتح في العمرة، وما روينا كان في حجة الوداع؛ ولأنه غير متطيب بعد الإحرام وهو المنهي عنه، وما في جسده تابع لاتصاله به. (فتح)
And apply perfume [i.e., perfume your body if you have it, not your garment, with what remains perceptible. (T)] in the sunnah manner with whatever perfume you wish; due to what is reported from Aishah (may Allah be pleased with her) that she said: "I would perfume the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) for his ihram with the best perfume I could find," narrated by Bukhari and Muslim. Muhammad and Zufar disliked (karaha) applying perfume with what remains perceptible after ihram, because if he sweats, it transfers to another part of his body, so it would be like beginning perfuming anew. And al-Shafi'i also held this view, due to his (peace be upon him) statement to a man in ihram who asked about the perfume on him: "As for the perfume on you, wash it off three times." And our proof is what is reported from Aishah (may Allah be pleased with her) that when he (peace be upon him) wanted to enter ihram, he would perfume himself with the best perfume he could find, and then I would see the glistening of the perfume, and in a narration: the glistening of oil on his head and beard. Also from her: she said: "We would go out with him (peace be upon him) to Makkah and apply musk mixed with perfume on our foreheads at ihram, and if one of us sweated, it would flow onto her face, and he would see it and not forbid us." And what (the opponent) narrated is abrogated because it was in the Year of Conquest during umrah, and what we narrated was during the Farewell Pilgrimage. And because he is not applying perfume after ihram – which is what is prohibited – and what is on his body is a consequence of its attachment to him. (Fath)
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding applying perfume before entering ihram. The author states that it is sunnah to apply perfume to the body (not the garment) with a substance that leaves a trace, based on the hadith of Aishah that she perfumed the Prophet for his ihram. This is a dalil from authentic hadith.

Then the commentator mentions an intra-Hanafi dispute: Muhammad and Zufar consider it disliked (makruh) to have a perfume residue that remains perceptible after ihram, because sweat may transfer it to another spot, resembling renewed application after ihram. Imam al-Shafi'i also holds this view, citing the Prophet's command to a man already in ihram to wash off the perfume three times.

The Hanafi response (li-lana) counters with stronger evidence: Aishah's report that the Prophet applied perfume before ihram and the glistening was visible on his head and beard after entering ihram. Also, women would apply musk on their foreheads and he did not prohibit them when sweat caused it to run. The opposing hadith is considered abrogated (mansukh) because it occurred earlier in the Year of Conquest (8 AH) during umrah, whereas the Hanafi evidence is from the Farewell Pilgrimage (10 AH). Moreover, the prohibition is only for applying perfume after ihram, not for perfume applied before that remains attached to the body.

The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the Hanafi view that applying perfume before ihram is sunnah and the residue does not harm, based on the practice of the Prophet and the abrogation of the opposing narration.

Key Terms
التطيب (al-tatayyub): Applying perfume to the body (not garment) before entering ihram.
النسخ (al-naskh): Abrogation of an earlier ruling by a later one; here the earlier hadith is superseded by later practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It was narrated by a weak chain
B) It was from the Year of Conquest (umrah) while the Prophet's practice in the Farewell Pilgrimage is later
C) It contradicts the Quran
D) It was only said to one person, not a general ruling

Key Takeaway
Applying perfume before ihram is sunnah and the presence of its residue after ihram does not violate the prohibition because it was applied before entering the state.

The Two Rak'ahs Before Ihram: Ruling and Supplication
Ruling on praying two rak'ahs and supplication before ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of the two rak'ahs before ihram, identify their basis in Quran and Sunnah, and describe the prescribed supplication.

Core Idea
The two rak'ahs before ihram are a sunnah prayer seeking divine help, based on the Prophet's practice and Quranic command.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq outlines two recommended acts before entering ihram: praying two rak'ahs and making a specific supplication. Understanding their basis and conditions ensures you perform them correctly, recognizing they are a sunnah, not an obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text states these two rak'ahs are 'nadb' (recommended). Determine that the Hanafi ruling is sunnah, not fard or wajib.
The command is interpreted as recommendation, not obligation.
2
Locate the evidence
The basis is the Prophet's action at Dhu al-Hulayfah (hadith) and the Quranic verse 2:45 commanding seeking help through prayer.
The hadith is narrated by Jabir; the Quranic verse is general.
3
Determine the conditions
The prayer is performed after wearing ihram garments and applying perfume, and must be outside the disliked times for prayer.
Times of karahah are sunrise, zenith, and sunset.
4
Understand the supplication
After the prayer, one says: 'Allahumma inni urid al-hajj fayassirhu li wa taqabbalhu minni' (O Allah, I intend Hajj, make it easy for me and accept it from me).
The supplication asks for ease and acceptance, following the example of Ibrahim and Isma'il.
5
Note the flexibility
The two rak'ahs can be fulfilled by the obligatory prayer (fard) or the greeting of the mosque (tahiyyah) if performed at the same time.
This shows the act is sunnah, not mandatory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(ط، ع)] لما روى جابر عنه أن النبي عليه صلى بذي الحليفة ركعتين عند إحرامه وهذه صلاة الاستعانة، وهي واجبة في جميع الأمور؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَاسْتَعِينُوا بِالصَّبْرِ وَالصَّلاةِ﴾ (البقرة: ٤٥) والحج أشق الأمور وأعظمها فيستعان له، وتجزئ عن هذين الركعتين المكتوبة والتحية، ولو قرأ فيهما بالكافرون والإخلاص لكان أفضل والأمر هنا للندب، وقيل: لبيان السنة. And pray two rak'ahs after wearing the garments and applying perfume, recommended outside the times of dislike. (T, A) Due to what Jabir narrated: that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed two rak'ahs at Dhu al-Hulayfah at his ihram. This is the prayer of seeking help, and it is obligatory in all matters due to His saying: 'And seek help through patience and prayer' (al-Baqarah: 45). And hajj is the most difficult and greatest of matters, so one seeks help through it. The obligatory prayer and the greeting of the mosque suffice for these two rak'ahs. If he recites in them Surah al-Kafirun and Surah al-Ikhlas, it is better. The command here is for recommendation, and it is said for clarification of sunnah. (Fath, Mustakhlas) 'Make it easy for me' etc. because its performance is in scattered times and diverse places, so asking for ease is appropriate. Similarly in Umrah, and asking for acceptance follows the example of al-Khalil (Ibrahim) and Isma'il (peace be upon them) when they said: 'Our Lord, accept from us' (al-Baqarah: 127). (Fath) 'From me': because Anas narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed Dhuhr then mounted his riding beast and said: 'O Allah, I intend Hajj' etc. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage covers two recommended acts before ihram: praying two rak'ahs and reciting a specific supplication. The two rak'ahs are prayed after wearing the ihram garments and applying perfume, and they should be performed outside of times when prayer is disliked (like sunrise, zenith, sunset). The basis is the Prophet's practice at Dhu al-Hulayfah. This prayer is called the prayer of seeking help (salat al-isti'anah), based on the Quranic verse commanding seeking help through patience and prayer. Since hajj is a major undertaking, this prayer is especially recommended. It can replace the two rak'ahs of the obligatory prayer (if one prays them at that time) or the greeting of the mosque (tahiyyah). It is best to recite Surah al-Kafirun and al-Ikhlas in these rak'ahs. The command is understood as recommendation (nadb), not obligation (wujub).

After the prayer, one says the supplication: 'Allahumma inni urid al-hajj fayassirhu li wa taqabbalhu minni' (O Allah, I intend Hajj, so make it easy for me and accept it from me). This asking for ease is fitting given the many times and places of hajj. Asking for acceptance follows the example of Ibrahim and Isma'il. The supplication is sunnah, based on the narration of Anas that the Prophet said this after Dhuhr prayer before setting out.

Key Terms
صلاة الاستعانة (salat al-isti'anah): Prayer of seeking help, specifically the two rak'ahs before ihram, based on Quran 2:45.
الندب (al-nadb): Recommendation; an act one is encouraged to do but not obligated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
The two rak'ahs before ihram are a sunnah based on the Prophet's practice and Quranic guidance, not an obligation; they can be replaced by other prayers and are accompanied by a supplication asking for ease and acceptance.

The Talbiyah: Ruling, Timing, and Meaning
Ruling and meaning of the Talbiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the Talbiyah, its recommended and permissible timings, explain the role of intention, and interpret the meaning of 'Labbayk'.

Core Idea
The Talbiyah is a sunnah to be recited immediately after the prayer, intended for Hajj, and commemorates the primordial response to Ibrahim's call.

The Talbiyah ('Labbayk Allahumma Labbayk') is the iconic chant of the pilgrim. This lesson unpacks its ruling in the Hanafi school: when to recite it, what intention is required, and the profound meaning behind the words. The passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, with its commentaries, guides us through both the practical sunnah and the spiritual reminder that the pilgrim is answering a call from Allah that echoes through time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Command and Its Strength
The text opens with an imperative ('لب') – a command to recite the Talbiyah after the prayer. Determine whether this command indicates obligation (fard/wajib) or recommendation (sunnah) in normal circumstances.
The command is interpreted as sunnah because it is linked to a specific time (after prayer) and there is no penalty for delay.
2
Distinguish Best Timing from Permissible Timing
Two narrations are presented: one for reciting after the prayer (preferred by Ibn Abbas) and another for reciting after mounting the riding beast. Analyse which is the best (afdal) and which is merely permissible (ja'iz).
The text states the first is best, but the second is also valid, showing flexibility.
3
Understand the Role of Intention (Niyyah)
The pronoun in 'tanwi biha' refers to the Talbiyah – one must intend the Hajj or Umrah when reciting. The text emphasizes that intention is a condition (shart) for all acts of worship, but verbal utterance is not a condition; the inner resolve suffices.
Intention is fard for ihram; reciting Talbiyah without intention does not constitute ihram.
4
Analyse the Linguistic Meaning of 'Labbayk'
The word 'Labbayk' is derived from 'labba' (to stay) in the dual form, indicating continuous and repeated obedience. The accusative case implies an implied verb: 'I am staying in Your obedience.'
This grammatical analysis reinforces that the pilgrim is committing to unwavering submission.
5
Reflect on the Spiritual Significance
The text explains that the Talbiyah is a response to the call of Prophet Ibrahim (as) when he proclaimed Hajj to humanity. Allah made his voice reach all souls destined to perform Hajj, and they answered 'Labbayk'. Reciting it now is a renewal of that pre-eternal covenant.
This elevates the Talbiyah from a mere phrase to an act of profound spiritual connection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And recite the Talbiyah immediately after your prayer [command from talbiyah, i.e., say 'Labbayk' etc. (Ayni)] because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) recited the Talbiyah after a prayer. This indicates the best way, so even if he recited after his riding beast stood up, it is permissible. There are narrations that he recited after his riding beast stood up, and these are more authentic and numerous, but it is narrated from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said: 'By Allah! He (the Prophet) made it binding upon himself – i.e., he recited the Talbiyah – in his prayer place.' (Ayni) 'Labbayk' etc. [i.e., I am staying firm in Your obedience. (Ayni)] It is a dual form from 'labba bil-makan', i.e., he stayed, and it is in the accusative with an implied verb meaning 'I am staying in obedience to You, staying after staying', i.e., constant attachment to Your obedience, as explained in grammar books. In the legislation of the talbiyah, there is a reminder of Allah's honor to His servants: that their coming (to Hajj) is by His summons. This is a response to the call of al-Khalil (Ibrahim) when Allah commanded him to proclaim the Hajj to the people. He stood at the Maqam and called: 'O servants of Allah! Commentary
This passage explains the Talbiyah, its timing, and its profound meaning. The author commands to recite the Talbiyah ('Labbayk Allahumma Labbayk...') immediately after the two rak'ahs of prayer. This is the sunnah way, confirmed by the Prophet's action. However, it is also permissible to recite it after mounting the riding beast, as some authentic narrations indicate. The best is to recite it in the prayer place, as Ibn Abbas emphasized.

The pronoun in 'tanwi biha' refers to the Talbiyah, meaning one should intend the hajj/umrah with the Talbiyah. Intention in the heart is essential; verbal utterance is not a condition, but combining both is better. Intention is the condition for all acts of worship.

The word 'Labbayk' is explained: it is a dual form from 'labb' meaning 'to stay', implying continuous and repeated obedience. It is an answer to Ibrahim's call, which Allah made heard by all souls destined for Hajj from pre-eternity. Thus, by reciting Talbiyah, the pilgrim responds to that primordial summons.

Key Terms
التلبية (al-talbiyah): The phrase 'Labbayk Allahumma Labbayk...' recited by the pilgrim, expressing response to Allah's call.
نية (niyyah): Intention in the heart for the act of worship; condition for validity of ihram.
لبيك (labbayk): The first word of the Talbiyah; dual form meaning 'I am staying (in obedience)' indicating continuous commitment.

Key Takeaway
The Talbiyah is a sunnah act recited best immediately after the prayer, and it carries deep spiritual meaning as a response to Prophet Ibrahim's call.

Recommended Acts Before Ihram: Perfume and Two Rak'ahs
Explains the sunan acts of applying perfume and praying two rak'ahs before ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on applying perfume before ihram and explain the evidence, and describe the ruling on praying two rak'ahs before ihram.

Core Idea
Apply perfume before ihram; its trace is fine; pray two rak'ahs seeking help.

Before entering the state of ihram, the pilgrim is encouraged to perform certain sunan acts. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies two such acts: applying perfume to the body and praying two rak'ahs. There is a known intra-Hanafi disagreement about the perfume: Abu Hanifa permits it even if a trace remains, while Muhammad and Zufar consider it makruh. Both rulings are supported by hadith evidence, and we will examine how the Hanafi school resolved this difference. The two rak'ahs are a recommended prayer of seeking help, and the passage explains its basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunan acts
Read the passage and list the recommended acts mentioned before ihram: applying perfume, praying two rak'ahs, and making the intention supplication.
The passage focuses on the first two; the supplication is briefly mentioned.
2
Analyze the evidence for perfume and the intra-Hanafi dispute
Locate the hadith cited by Abu Hanifa (from Aisha) and the opposing evidence from Muhammad/Zufar (the washing hadith). Compare the two and understand why Abu Hanifa's view is preferred (abrogation argument).
3
Determine the mufta bihi position for perfume
Based on the tarjih given in the commentar, state that the relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's: applying perfume before ihram is Sunnah and its trace does not invalidate the ihram.
This is despite the opposition of Muhammad, Zufar, and al-Shafi'i.
4
Analyze the evidence for the two rak'ahs
Identify the source for the two rak'ahs: the hadith of Jabir and the Quranic verse on seeking help. Determine the ruling: sunnah (recommended) and note that it suffices for other sunan prayers.
The command is interpreted as recommendation (nadb), not obligation.
5
Apply to a practical scenario
Imagine a pilgrim applies perfume before ihram, then enters ihram. The scent is still detectable. Explain the Hanafi ruling and why it differs from the Shafi'i view.
This highlights the thamarah al-khilaf: the practical consequence of the differing opinions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج
كيفية الإحرام
وتطيب وصل ركعتين، وقل: اللهم إني أريد الحجّ فيسره لي وتقبله مني، ولبّ دُبُرَ صلاتك تنوي بها الحج، وهي: لبيك اللهم لبيك، لبيك لا شريك لك لبيك، وهي الركعتان المذكورتان التلبية
وتطيب [ أي طيب بدنك إن وجدت لا ثوبك بما تبقى عينه. (ط)] على وجه السنة بأي طيب شئت؛ لما ورد عن عائشة ما أنها قالت: "كنت أطيب رسول الله له بأطيب ما أجد"، رواه البخاري ومسلم، وكره محمد وزفر بما تبقى عينه بعد الإحرام؛ لأنه إذا عرق ينتقل إلى محل آخر من بدنه، فيكون بمنزلة ابتداء التطيب، و به قال الشافعي أيضاً؛ لقوله عليه للرجل محرم سأله عما كان عليه من الطيب: "أما الطيب الذي بك فاغسله ثلاث مرات"، ولنا : ما ورد عن عائشة لها أنه عليه كان إذا أراد أن يحرم يتطيب بأطيب ما يجد، ثم أرى وبيص الطيب، وفي رواية: وبيص الدهن في رأسه ولحيته، وعنها أيضاً أنها قالت: كنا نخرج معه عليه إلى مكة فنضمد جباهنا بالمسك المطيب عند الإحرام، فإذا عرقت إحدانا سال على وجهها فيراه عليه، ولا ينهانا عنه، وما رواه منسوخ؛ لأنه كان في عام الفتح في العمرة، وما روينا كان في حجة الوداع؛ ولأنه غير متطيب بعد الإحرام وهو المنهي عنه، وما في جسده تابع لاتصاله به. (فتح) صل ركعتين بعد اللبس والتطيب ندبا في غير وقت كراهة. (ط، ع)] لما روى جابر عنه أن النبي عليه صلى بذي الحليفة ركعتين عند إحرامه وهذه صلاة الاستعانة، وهي واجبة في جميع الأمور؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَاسْتَعِينُوا بِالصَّبْرِ وَالصَّلاةِ (البقرة: (٤٥) والحج أشق الأمور وأعظمها فيستعان له، وتجزئ عن هذين الركعتين المكتوبة والتحية، ولو قرأ فيهما بالكافرون والإخلاص لكان أفضل والأمر هنا للندب، وقيل: لبيان السنة. (فتح، مستخلص) فيسره لي إلخ لأن أداءه في أزمنة متفرقة وأماكن متباينة فناسب سؤال التيسير فيه، وكذا في العمرة، وسؤال القبول لموافقة الخليل وإسماعيل عليهما السلام حيث قالا : رَبَّنَا تَقَبَّلْ مِنَّا ﴾ (البقرة: ۱۲۷) (فتح) مني: لأن أنسا روى أنه عليه صلى الظهر ثم ركب على راحلته فقال: "اللهم إني أريد الحج" إلخ. (عيني)
The Book of Hajj. The manner of Ihram. Apply perfume, pray two rak'ahs, and say: O Allah, I intend Hajj, so make it easy for me and accept it from me. Recite the talbiyah after your prayer intending Hajj, and it is: Labbayk Allahumma Labbayk, Labbayka la sharika laka Labbayk. And the two rak'ahs are mentioned [as the talbiyah]. Apply perfume [i.e., perfume your body if you have it, not your garment, with something whose trace remains (line)] in the manner of the Sunnah with any perfume you wish; based on what is narrated from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that she said: 'I used to perfume the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) with the best perfume I could find,' narrated by Bukhari and Muslim. And Muhammad and Zufar disliked [perfume] whose trace remains after ihram; because if he sweats it transfers to another place on his body, thus it is like beginning to apply perfume, and al-Shafi'i also said this; due to his (peace be upon him) statement to the man who was in ihram and asked about the perfume on him: 'As for the perfume on you, wash it three times.' Our evidence: what is narrated from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that he (peace be upon him) when he wanted to enter ihram would apply the best perfume he could find, then I would see the shine of the perfume, and in a narration: the shine of oil on his head and beard. And from her also that she said: 'We used to go out with him (peace be upon him) to Mecca and we would apply musk to our foreheads at ihram, and when one of us would sweat, it would run down her face and he would see it and not forbid us.' And what he narrated is abrogated; because it was in the year of the conquest during Umrah, and what we narrated was during the Farewell Hajj. And because he is not applying perfume after ihram, which is what is prohibited, and what is on his body is a result of its contact [before ihram]. (Fath). Pray two rak'ahs after wearing [ihram garments] and applying perfume, recommended, not at a disliked time. (T, A). Based on what Jabir narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed two rak'ahs at Dhu al-Hulayfah at his ihram, and this is the prayer of seeking help, and it is obligatory in all matters; due to His statement: 'And seek help through patience and prayer' (al-Baqarah:45). And Hajj is the most difficult and greatest of matters, so one seeks help for it. And it suffices for these two rak'ahs the obligatory prayer and the greeting of the mosque. If he recites in them al-Kafirun and al-Ikhlas, that is better. And the command here is for recommendation, and it is said: for clarifying the Sunnah. (Fath, Mustakhlis). 'Make it easy for me etc.' because performing it at different times and places befits asking for ease, and similarly in Umrah, and asking for acceptance to follow the example of al-Khalil and Ismail (peace be upon them) when they said: 'Our Lord, accept from us' (al-Baqarah:127). (Fath). 'From me': because Anas narrated that he (peace be upon him) prayed Zuhr then mounted his mount and said: 'O Allah, I intend Hajj' etc. (Ayni).
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage describes the Sunnah acts recommended before entering the state of ihram for Hajj. The author includes three actions: applying perfume (tayyib), praying two rak'ahs, and making the intention supplication. The commentary expands on each. First, perfume: Abu Hanifa holds that one may apply perfume before ihram even if its trace remains after entering ihram, based on the hadith of Aisha that the Prophet would apply perfume and its shine was visible. Muhammad al-Shaybani and Zufar, along with al-Shafi'i, consider this disliked because any remaining trace after ihram is like a new application. Abu Hanifa's view is preferred and is the relied-upon position. The two rak'ahs: it is a Sunnah to pray two rak'ahs with the intention of seeking help (salat al-isti'anah) after donning the ihram garments and applying perfume. The commentator notes it is mustahabb (recommended) and that the command in the hadith indicates recommendation, not obligation. These two rak'ahs can substitute for the sunnah of the time or the tahiyyat al-masjid. It is better to recite Surat al-Kafirun and al-Ikhlas. The supplication 'Allahumma inni uridu al-hajj...' is the intention, and it is also recommended. The commentator notes that asking for ease and acceptance follows the example of Ibrahim and Ismail. Thus, these acts prepare the pilgrim for the sacred state.

Key Terms
التطيب (al-tayyib): Applying perfume to the body before ihram, a recommended act.
الركعتان (al-rak'atan): Two rak'ahs of prayer performed before ihram, sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on applying perfume that leaves a trace before entering ihram?
A) It is makruh because the trace remains after ihram.
B) It is Sunnah and permissible; the trace is not a new application.
C) It is haram because perfume is prohibited in ihram.
D) It is only allowed if the perfume is unscented.

Key Takeaway
Apply perfume before ihram is Sunnah; the trace is fine. Pray two rak'ahs after dressing and perfuming.

The Prohibitions of Ihram: Rafath, Fusuq, and Jidal
Defines the three prohibitions of ihram and provides their Quranic basis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three prohibitions of ihram, define each one, and explain the Hanafi position on the scope of fusuq.

Core Idea
The Quran forbids rafath, fusuq, and jidal in Hajj; the Hanafi school defines fusuq as all sins.

The state of ihram is a sacred period during which a pilgrim must avoid certain acts. The Quran explicitly prohibits three categories: rafath, fusuq, and jidal. In this lesson, we examine their meanings, the difference of opinion on fusuq, and the legal ruling derived from the verse.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verse
The verse (2:197) states the prohibitions directly. Note that it uses a report form but is interpreted as a prohibition.
The verse is the primary evidence.
2
Define rafath
Identify the different interpretations: sexual intercourse, or obscene speech. The Hanafi view includes both.
The text mentions three possible definitions.
3
Define fusuq
Understand the two opinions: cursing vs all sins. The correct Hanafi view is all sins, narrated from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar.
The passage declares this view as 'as-sahih'.
4
Define jidal
Jidal is argumentation that leads to anger. However, religious debate with evidence is exempt.
The exception is important.
5
Derive the ruling
All three are haram during ihram. The prohibition is from the Quran.
This is a direct ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فاتق الرفث [ أي اجتنب الجماع ، وقيل : الكلام الفاحش (ط، ع)] الرفث الوقاع ، وقيل : ذكره بدواعيه عند النساء، وقيل: الكلام الفاحش الذي خوطب به النساء، والفسوق الخروج عن طاعة الله تعالى، واختلف في المراد هنا، قيل: السباب؛ لقوله : "سباب المؤمن فسوق"، وروي عن ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما وابن عمر رضي الله عنهما أن المراد هنا المعاصي كلها، وهو الصحيح؛ لأن ذلك كله خروج عن الطاعة، والجدال أن تجادل غيرك مجادلة تفضي إلى التغاضب وزوال التألف، وأما الجدال على وجه النظر في أمر من أمور الدين بالدليل فلا بأس، وأصل الكل قوله تعالى: ﴿فَمَنْ فَرَضَ فِيهِنَّ الْحَجَّ فَلا رَفَثَ وَلَا فُسُوقَ وَلَا جِدَالَ فِي الْحَجَّ ﴾ (البقرة: ۱۹۷)، وهذا خبر بمعنى النهي، أي لا ترفثوا ولا تفسقوا ولا تجادلوا. (فتح)
So avoid rafath [i.e., avoid sexual intercourse, and it is said: obscene speech (T, A)]. Rafath means sexual intercourse, and it is said: mentioning it with its motives in front of women, and it is said: obscene speech addressed to women. Fusuq is leaving the obedience of Allah Almighty, and there is a difference of opinion about what is meant here. It is said: cursing; due to his (peace be upon him) statement: 'Cursing a believer is fisq.' And it is narrated from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them) that what is meant here is all sins, and this is correct, because all of that is leaving obedience. Jidal is that you argue with others in a way that leads to anger and loss of harmony. As for arguing for the purpose of examining a matter of religion with evidence, there is no harm. The basis of all is the statement of Allah Almighty: 'So whoever undertakes Hajj in them, let there be no rafath, nor fusuq, nor jidal in Hajj' (al-Baqarah:197). This is a report in the form of a prohibition, i.e., do not commit rafath, nor fusuq, nor jidal. (Fath)
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage explains the three major prohibitions during the state of ihram, derived from the Quranic verse in Surah al-Baqarah. The commentator provides definitions. Rafath primarily refers to sexual intercourse, and by extension, any talk about it. The stronger opinion is that it includes both the act and obscene speech. Fusuq means disobedience to Allah, and while some restrict it to name-calling, the correct view (as narrated from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar) is that it includes all sins – hence the pilgrim must avoid any sin during ihram. Jidal is defined as contentious argumentation that leads to anger and broken relations, but argumentation for seeking religious truth is exempted. The verse is understood as a prohibition, meaning these actions are forbidden. This serves as a reminder of the special sanctity of the state of ihram.

Key Terms
الرفث (al-rafath): Sexual intercourse, and by extension, obscene talk about it.
الفسوق (al-fusuq): All acts of disobedience to Allah; specifically during ihram, all sins are prohibited.
الجدال (al-jidal): Argumentation that leads to anger and loss of harmony; religious discussion with evidence is exempt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the correct interpretation of 'fusuq' in the context of ihram?
A) Only cursing and abusive language.
B) All sins and disobedience to Allah.
C) Only major sins like murder.
D) Only breaking the fast intentionally.

Key Takeaway
The three prohibitions of ihram (rafath, fusuq, jidal) are all haram, with fusuq encompassing all sins.

The Talbiyah: Formula and Role in Entering Ihram
Explanation of talbiyah formula and requirement of talbiyah with niyyah for ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the talbiyah, explain why additions are permissible, and identify the conditions for entering ihram.

Core Idea
Talbiyah with intention is required to enter ihram; intention alone is insufficient in the Hanafi school.

This lesson examines the talbiyah — the declaration that initiates the sacred state of ihram. The passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies both the wording of the talbiyah and its legal status. You will see how the Hanafi school determines what is required to enter ihram, and why additions to the talbiyah are not only allowed but recommended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the talbiyah formula
Read the opening of the passage: 'Indeed praise and favor belong to You...' This is the sunnah talbiyah. Understand that the Hanafi school considers this formula as transmitted from the Prophet (peace be upon him).
The grammatical discussion of 'inna' (kasr vs. fath) is a side point; focus on the ruling.
2
Analyze the ruling on adding to the talbiyah
The text says 'add to it and do not diminish.' Recognize that the Hanafi school permits additions. Compare with the Shafi'i objection by analogy to adhan. Note the Hanafi response: talbiyah is for worship, not announcement.
The hadith of Ibn 'Umar and Ibn Mas'ud are key proofs.
3
Recognize the requirement for entering ihram
The matn states: 'When you recite the talbiyah with intention, you have entered ihram.' The commentary emphasizes that both intention and talbiyah are needed. Identify the opposing views (Abu Yusuf, Shafi'i) and their analogies.
The Quranic verse 2:197 and the analogy to takbirat al-ihram are used as proofs.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
The text clearly states that the relied-upon position is that talbiyah is wajib and intention alone is not enough. Note that a substitute word of exaltation in any language suffices because Hajj has broader scope than prayer.
This is the fatwa that a Hanafi mufti would issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج
محظورات الإحرام
إنَّ الحَمدَ والنّعمَةَ لَكَ والملكَ لا شَريكَ لك، وزد فيها ولا تنقص، فإذا لبيت ناوياً
بكسر الهمزة وفتحها
فقد أحرمت، فاتق الرّفث .
كرر للتأكيد
في التلبية ندبا
أو سقت الهدي
مرة حج مرة، ومن زاد في التلبية حج مراراً، وقوله: "إن الحمد" بكسر الهمزة وهو قول الفراء، وقال الكسائي: الفتح أحسن ومعناه لأن "الحمد" أو "بأن الحمد"، وعن ابن سماعة قلت لمحمد ما أحب إليك؟ قال: الكسر للابتداء والفتح للبناء والابتداء أولى من البناء، أي ليكون ابتداء ذكر لا تعليلاً للكلام الأول.
تتمة: الأنبياء ان كانوا يلبون إذا حجوا، فيونس بن متى عليه كان يقول: لبيك فراج الكربة، وكان موسى يقول : لبيك أنا عبدك لديك، وكان عيسى علي يقول : لبيك أنا عبدك أنا ابن أمتك. (مسكين، فتح، مستخلص) والنعمة بكسر النون كل ما يصل إلى الخلق من النفع ودفع الضرر. (عيني) والملك: بضم الميم وفسر بأنه سعة المقدور . (عيني) وزد فيها وقال الشافعي في رواية الربيع عنه: لا يزيد؛ لأنه ذكر منظوم فتخل به الزيادة والنقصان كالأذان، ولنا: أن ابن عمر ما كان يقول إذا استوت به راحلته زيادة على المروي: "لبيك لبيك وسعديك، والخير بين يديك، والرغباء إليك والعمل"، متفق عليه، وعن ابن مسعود له أنه كان يقول: "لبيك بعدد التراب لبيك"، ولأن المقصود هو الثناء وإظهار العبودية فلا يمنع الزيادة عليه بخلاف الأذان؛ لأنه للإعلام، فلا يزاد على المنقول، وقوله: "ولا تنقص؛ لأنه هو المنقول عنه عليا باتفاق الرواة، وقال علي: "خذوا مناسككم عني"، فالنقص مکروه اتفاقاً. (فتح) ناوياً: أي حال كونك ناوياً للحج. (ط،ع) فقد أحرمت: [ أي دخلت في الإحرام وصرت محرما. (مستخلص)] هذا تصريح بأنه يكون شارعاً عند وجود النية والتلبية، وإشارة إلى أنه لا يصير محرما بمجرد النية ما لم يأت بالتلبية، وعن أبي يوسف أنه يصير شارعا بالنية وحدها، وبه قال الشافعي؛ لأن الشروع بالنية كالصوم، ولنا قوله تعالى: ﴿فَمَنْ فَرَضَ فِيهِنَّ الْحَجَّ ﴾ (البقرة: ۱۹۷) قال ابن عباس لما فرض الحج الإهلال، وقال ابن عمر الهما: التلبية، وقال ابن مسعود الله: الإحرام، وقالت عائشة هما: لا إحرام إلا لمن أهل ولبى؛ ولأنه عقد للأداء فلا بد من ذكر كما في تحريمة الصلاة، ويصير شارعاً بذكر ما يقصد به التعظيم سوى التلبية فارسية كانت أو عربية؛ لأن باب الحج أوسع من باب الصلاة حتى يقام غير الذكر مقام الذكر كتقليد البدن بخلاف الصوم؛ لأنه ركن واحد [ رمز الحقائق: ١٥٣/١] (مستخلص)
The Book of Hajj. Prohibitions of Ihram. 'Indeed praise and favor belong to You, and the dominion, there is no partner with You.' And add to it and do not diminish. When you recite the talbiyah with intention, you have entered ihram. So be mindful of ar-rafath. (Repeat for emphasis, in the talbiyah as a recommend act. Or if you drive a sacrificial animal, perform hajj once. And whoever adds to the talbiyah performs hajj many times.) And his saying: 'Inna al-hamda' with kasr of the hamzah is the saying of al-Farra', and al-Kisa'i said: the fath is better and its meaning is because 'al-hamd' or 'bi-anna al-hamd'. And from Ibn Sama'ah: I said to Muhammad: which do you prefer? He said: kasr is for beginning and fath is for building, and beginning is better than building, i.e., to be a beginning of remembrance, not a reason for the first speech. Appendix: The prophets used to recite talbiyah when they performed hajj. Yunus ibn Matta used to say: 'Labbayk, remover of distress.' Musa used to say: 'Labbayk, I am Your servant, with You.' 'Isa used to say: 'Labbayk, I am Your servant, I am the son of Your maidservant.' (Miskin, Fath, Mustakhlas) And al-ni'mah with kasr of the nun: everything that reaches creation of benefit and repulsion of harm. (Ayni) And al-mulk with damm of the mim: explained as capacity of power. (Ayni) 'And add to it'—al-Shafi'i in one narration from al-Rabi' said: he should not add, because it is an organized remembrance, so adding and subtracting would break it like the adhan. Our proof: Ibn 'Umar used to say when his mount stood with him, in addition to the transmitted version: 'Labbayka Labbayka wa Sa'dayka, wal-khayru bayda yadayka, war-raghba'u ilayka wal-'amal', agreed upon. And from Ibn Mas'ud that he used to say: 'Labbayka bi-'adadi t-turabi Labbayka'. And because the purpose is praise and showing servitude, so addition is not prevented, unlike the adhan because it is for announcement, so nothing is added to what is transmitted. And his saying: 'and do not diminish' because it is transmitted from 'Ali by agreement of narrators, and 'Ali said: 'Take your rituals from me', so diminution is makruh by agreement. (Fath) 'With intention': i.e., while you are intending Hajj. (T, A) 'You have entered ihram': i.e., you have entered into ihram and become a muhrim. (Mustakhlas) This is an explicit statement that he becomes a starter when intention and talbiyah exist, and an indication that he does not become a muhrim with intention alone unless he performs the talbiyah. And from Abu Yusuf that he becomes a starter with intention alone, and al-Shafi'i said the same, because starting with intention is like fasting. Our proof: His statement ﴿So whoever has determined (farada) therein the Hajj﴾ (al-Baqarah: 197). Ibn 'Abbas said: when he determines Hajj, it is al-ihlal. Ibn 'Umar said: al-talbiyah. Ibn Mas'ud said: al-ihram. And 'A'ishah said: There is no ihram except for one who raises his voice and recites talbiyah. And because it is a contract for performance, so a mention is necessary as in the takbirat al-ihram of prayer. And he becomes a starter with any mention intended for exaltation other than the talbiyah, whether Persian or Arabic, because the domain of hajj is broader than that of prayer, such that a non-mention is made to stand in place of mention, like taqlid of the sacrificial animal, unlike fasting because it is a single pillar. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/153) (Mustakhlas)
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains two connected rulings: the wording and ruling of the talbiyah, and the conditions for entering ihram. The matn first presents the sunnah talbiyah formula. The commentary then discusses the proper pronunciation of 'inna al-hamda' (with kasr or fath) and the permissibility of adding to it. The Hanafi school allows additions because the purpose is praise and worship, and there are reports of the Companions adding phrases. Imam al-Shafi'i's objection based on analogy to the adhan is rejected because the adhan is for information, while talbiyah is for worship; thus additions are praiseworthy. Omitting parts of the transmitted talbiyah is agreed by consensus to be makruh. Then the passage addresses the start of ihram: the matn states that when one recites the talbiyah with intention, one has entered ihram. The commentary clarifies that both intention and talbiyah are required. Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that intention alone suffices, analogizing to fasting. The Hanafi response relies on the Quranic verse 'So whoever has determined (farada) therein the Hajj...' understood by Ibn 'Abbas as al-ihlal (talbiyah), and also the analogy to the takbirat al-ihram in salah. The relied-upon position is that both intention and talbiyah are necessary. The commentary also notes that any word of exaltation can substitute for the talbiyah in Arabic or Persian, because the domain of Hajj is broader than that of salah.

Key Terms
التلبية (at-talbiyah): The verbal declaration 'Labbayk...' that initiates the state of ihram.
الإحرام (al-ihram): The sacred state entered for Hajj or 'Umrah, with prohibitions.
النية (an-niyyah): Intention to perform Hajj or 'Umrah, required for ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is required to enter the state of ihram?
A) Intention (niyyah) alone
B) Talbiyah alone
C) Both intention and talbiyah
D) Only wearing ihram garments

Key Takeaway
Talbiyah is wajib; it must accompany intention to enter ihram in the Hanafi school.

Prohibitions of Ihram: Rafath, Fusuq, Jidal, Hunting, and Garments
Explaining prohibitions of ihram with proofs and disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prohibitions of ihram, identify their proofs from Quran and Sunnah, and apply the Hanafi position on the dispute regarding safflower-dyed clothes.

Core Idea
Prohibitions of ihram derive from clear Quranic and prophetic commands; even pointing to game is prohibited if the hunter does not already know.

This lesson explains the key prohibitions that a muhrim must observe during Hajj and Umrah: sexual activity, sin, argument, hunting, wearing sewn garments, and using perfumed dyes. The commentary expands each prohibition with proofs and notes a difference of opinion with Shafi'i and Hanbali schools regarding safflower-dyed clothing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three verbal prohibitions
Locate the terms rafath, fusuq, and jidal in the source, and note their definitions and the Quranic basis (2:197). Understand that religious debate is excluded.
Fusuq is interpreted as all sins, especially cursing.
2
Understand the prohibition of hunting
Find the Quranic verse (5:95) prohibiting killing land game. Then examine the related prohibition of pointing to or leading a hunter to game.
The key nuance: pointing/leading is forbidden only when the hunter does not already know about the game.
3
Analyze the exception for pointing
Read the hadith of Abu Qatadah and the commentary: the prohibition is conditioned on the hunter's ignorance. If the hunter already knows, pointing is not prohibited.
This is based on the prophetic response: 'Did any of you command him or point?' They said no, so he allowed the meat.
4
List the prohibited sewn garments
From the hadith of Ibn 'Umar, identify the prohibited items: qamis, turban, burnus, sirwal, and the exception for khuffs (cut below ankles if no sandals).
Women are exempt from this prohibition; they may wear sewn clothes.
5
Examine the dispute on mu'asfar
Note that the Hanafi school prohibits clothes dyed with wars, za'faran, or 'usfur (safflower). The Shafi'i and Hanbali schools permit 'usfur because it lacks fragrance.
This is a non-issue within the Hanafi school; the mufta bihi is prohibition.

إلا أن أي واتق لبس الخفين إلا أن لا تجد. (مسكين) الكعبين أي المفصلين الذين وسط القدمين عند معقد شراك النعل، وهو سيره الذي على ظهر القدم، وهو المراد هنا بالكعب. (مسكين) بورس: نبات كالسمسم ليس إلا باليمن، يزرع فيبقى نحو عشرين سنة. (قاموس) أو عصفر وهو زهر القرطم، وقال الشافعي وأحمد: لا بأس بلبس المعصفر ؛ لأنه لا طيب له رمز الحقائق: ١٥٣/١]
So be mindful of ar-rafath: i.e., avoid sexual intercourse, and it is said: obscene speech (T, A). Ar-rafath is sexual intercourse, and it is said: mentioning it with its incitements to women, and it is said: obscene speech addressed to women. Al-fusuq is exiting from obedience to Allah, and there is disagreement on what is meant here; it is said: cursing because of his saying 'Cursing a believer is fusuq', and it is narrated from Ibn 'Abbas and Ibn 'Umar that what is meant here is all sins, and that is the correct view because all that is exiting from obedience. Al-jidal is that you argue with another person in a manner that leads to mutual anger and loss of harmony. As for argument for the purpose of examining a matter of religion with evidence, there is no harm. The basis of all is His statement: 'So whoever has determined therein the Hajj, let there be no rafath, no fusuq, and no jidal in the Hajj' (al-Baqarah 2:197). This is an indicative statement meaning prohibition: do not commit rafath, do not commit fusuq, and do not engage in jidal. (Fath) [Page 253] And al-fusuq, al-jidal, killing game, pointing to it, leading to it, wearing the qamis (shirt) (i.e., also be mindful of game) and also be mindful, and the sirwal (trousers), the turban, the skullcap, the qaba' (outer garment), and the khuffs (leather socks) unless you cannot find sandals, then cut them below the ankles, and the garment dyed with wars (a plant) or za'faran (saffron) or 'usfur (safflower). (i.e., also be mindful of wearing the garment, etc.) And al-fusuq: i.e., sins and exiting from obedience to Allah is ugly, and in the state of ihram it is uglier. (T, A) And al-jidal: i.e., quarrel with companions, servants, and camel drivers, and dispute with them and cursing. (Ayni) And killing game: i.e., also be mindful; because of His statement: 'And do not kill game while you are in ihram' (al-Ma'idah 5:95), i.e., land game. (T, A) And pointing to it: pointing occurs when the game is present. (Ayni) It is an apposition to his saying 'killing game'. The apparent import of it is that there is no difference in the prohibition of pointing and leading between whether the killer knows or not, but the preponderant view is that the prohibition is applied when he does not know about it. The basis for that is the hadith of Abu Qatadah: when they asked him about the meat of a wild donkey that Abu Qatadah had hunted, he said: 'Did any of you command him or point to it?' They said: 'No.' He said: 'Then eat what remains of his meat.' Narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim. He conditioned its permissibility on the absence of pointing to it. Similarly, leading removes the security from the game, so it is prohibited. (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 2/257) 'Alayhi: i.e., to the game, and it is when the game is absent. And the place of prohibition of both is when the killer does not know, not when he knows. (T) And wearing the qamis: includes al-zarwiyyah and al-burnus. The controlling principle here is that everything carried on the measure of the body or part of it such that it stays on its own by sewing or gluing or otherwise, constitutes wearing. Al-sirwal is non-Arabic, and its plural is sarawilat, and it is said: al-sarawil is plural of sirwal. And the turban and skullcap because wearing them necessitates covering the head, which is prohibited even if the middle of the head is exposed. And wearing al-qaba' (with alif) is to insert his shoulders and hands into its sleeves. If he does not insert, it is permissible as if he drapes a shirt or similar. And wearing the khuffs (dual) because wearing a single khuff is prohibited outside ihram also. This applies to men. As for women, they are allowed to wear khuffs. The basis for prohibiting these items is the hadith of Ibn 'Umar: he said: The Messenger of Allah was asked: What should the muhrim wear? He said: 'He should not wear the qamis, nor the turban, nor the burnus, nor the sirwal, nor anything touched with wars or za'faran, nor the khuffs, unless he cannot find sandals, then let him cut them so that they become below the ankles.' Agreed upon. Al-ka'b here is the joint in the middle of the foot at the point of the shoelace, as narrated by Hisham from Muhammad. (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 2/258) (Fath) 'Unless': i.e., be mindful of wearing khuffs unless you cannot find (sandals). (Miskin) Al-ka'bayn: i.e., the two joints that are in the middle of the feet at the point of the shoelace of the sandal, which is its strap on the top of the foot, and that is what is meant here by al-ka'b. (Miskin) Wars: a plant like sesame, found only in Yemen, it grows and lasts about twenty years. (Qamus) Or 'usfur: it is the flower of qurtum (safflower). Al-Shafi'i and Ahmad said: there is no harm in wearing mu'asfar (dyed with 'usfur) because it has no perfume. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/153)
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage enumerates the prohibitions of ihram, expanding the matn's list with proofs and disputes. The first three prohibitions—rafath (sexual activity or its verbal suggestion), fusuq (disobedience, especially cursing), and jidal (argument leading to anger)—are derived from the Quranic verse in al-Baqarah. The text clarifies that religious debate is excluded from the prohibition. Then the passage covers killing game (land animals), with the explicit Quranic prohibition. It also deals with pointing to game or leading a hunter to it; the Hanafi position is that this is prohibited only if the hunter does not already know about the game, based on a hadith of Abu Qatadah. If the hunter already knows, there is no prohibition. The next section covers sewn garments: the hadith of Ibn 'Umar prohibits the muhrim from wearing the qamis, turban, burnus, sirwal, and items touched with wars or za'faran, and also khuffs unless sandals are unavailable, in which case the khuffs must be cut below the ankles. The commentary specifies the definition of each garment, noting that the prohibition is for men; women may wear sewn clothes. For the khuffs, the exception is only for those who cannot find sandals. Finally, the discussion of dyes: the Hanafi school prohibits clothes dyed with wars, za'faran, or 'usfur (safflower), considering them perfumes. Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad permit 'usfur because it has no fragrance. The passage ends with that difference.

Key Terms
الرفث (ar-rafath): Sexual intercourse or its verbal mention with women.
الفسوق (al-fusuq): Disobedience to Allah, including all sins, with emphasis on cursing.
الجدال (al-jidal): Argument that leads to anger and loss of harmony; allowed if for religious discussion.
الصيد (as-sayd): Killing land game animals.
القميص (al-qamis): A sewn garment that covers the body; includes similar items like burnus and zarwiyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Permitted if the hunter does not see the pointing
D) Prohibited only if the hunter kills the game based on the pointing

Key Takeaway
The prohibitions of ihram are backed by clear Quran and hadith, and even ancillary actions like pointing to game are regulated to maintain the sanctity of Hajj.

Prohibition of Fusuq and Jidal in Ihram
Definition of prohibited acts in ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define fusuq and jidal in the Hanafi context and explain why their prohibition is intensified during ihram.

Core Idea
All sins and arguments are prohibited in ihram, and their gravity increases.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq elaborates on two prohibitions of the state of ihram: fusuq (general disobedience) and jidal (quarrelling). While both are blameworthy in general, the text stresses that during ihram they become even more severe. This lesson clarifies their precise meanings and legal implications for the pilgrim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibitions
State the two acts that are prohibited during ihram according to the passage: fusuq and jidal.
These are mentioned as part of the prohibitions for the muhrim.
2
Define fusuq
From the text, explain that fusuq refers to sins and disobedience to Allah, i.e., exiting from obedience.
The text says 'الفسوق: أي المعاصي والخروج عن طاعة الله تعالى'.
3
Define jidal
Explain that jidal includes quarreling, disputing, and verbal abuse with travel companions, servants, and mule-drivers.
The text specifies 'المخاصمة مع الرفقة والخدم والمكارين'.
4
Understand the intensification
Explain why the text says 'في حالة الإحرام أقبح' (in ihram it is uglier). This indicates that the sin is greater when committed in the state of ihram.
This is a common principle in Hanafi fiqh: the sacred state heightens the gravity of sins.
5
Apply the ruling
Conclude that both fusuq and jidal are haram during ihram, and that even minor arguments are included in the prohibition of jidal.
The text does not provide exceptions; the prohibition is general.

And fusuq: meaning sins and disobedience to Allah, may He be exalted, is ugly, and in the state of ihram it is uglier. (T., A.) And jidal: meaning quarreling with companions, servants, and mule-drivers, and disputing with them, and verbal abuse. (Ayni)

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the prohibitions of fusuq (sinning) and jidal (argumentation) during ihram. The commentator explains that fusuq refers to any sin or disobedience, which is inherently bad, but becomes even more severe when one is in the state of ihram. Jidal is defined as quarreling with travel companions, servants, or transport providers, including disputes and verbal abuse. The text does not provide explicit proofs here; rather, it is a direct explanation of the prohibitions listed in the matn.

Key Terms
الفسوق (al-fusūq): Sins and disobedience to Allah; exiting from obedience.
الجدال (al-jidāl): Quarreling, disputing, and verbal abuse with companions, servants, and mule-drivers.

Prohibition of Killing Game, Pointing and Indicating
Prohibits killing game, pointing to it, and indicating it, with proofs and conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on killing game during ihram and distinguish between prohibited pointing/indicating (when the hunter is unaware) and permissible cases.

Core Idea
Killing land game in ihram is haram; pointing or indicating is only prohibited if the hunter was unaware of the game.

This lesson tackles a key prohibition during ihram: hunting land game. The Quranic verse is clear, but the commentator expands on two related acts—pointing to game and indicating its location. The initial ruling seems absolute, but a deeper analysis reveals a crucial condition: the prohibition of these acts depends on whether the hunter already knows about the game. Understanding this nuance prevents over-application of the rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is killing land game (ṣayd) while in ihram. The ruling is haram, derived from the Quranic prohibition.
Sea game is not included; the prohibition is specific to land game.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The Quranic verse (al-Ma'idah 5:95) is the primary proof: 'Do not kill game while you are in a state of ihram.' The negative imperative indicates a clear prohibition.
The verse is qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalala.
3
Analyze the extension to pointing and indicating
The matn extends the prohibition to pointing (isharah) to present game and indicating (dalalah) the location of absent game. The initial apparent ruling treats them as absolutely prohibited.
Pointing is for game that is visible; indication is for hidden game.
4
Note the ikhtilaf and the hadith
The commentator presents a preponderant (rajih) view that the prohibition of pointing and indicating is conditional: it applies only when the killer had no prior knowledge of the game. The proof is the hadith of Abu Qatada, where the Prophet (saw) permitted the meat because no one had pointed or indicated, implying that if they had, it would be prohibited.
The hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The preponderant view (mufta bihi) is that pointing and indicating are haram only if the hunter was unaware. This restricts the broader absolute ruling, based on the hadith and the principle that prohibition tied to an act of assistance only applies when the assistance is effective.
If the hunter already knows, pointing does not cause the hunt; thus no prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقتل الصيد : أي اتق أيضاً؛ لقوله تعالى: ولا تَقْتُلُوا الصَّيْدَ وَأَنْتُمْ حُرُم (المائدة : ٩٥) أي الصيد البري. (ط،ع) والإشارة إليه والإشارة تكون فيما إذا كان الصيد حاضراً. (عيني) عطف على قوله: "قتل الصيد"، وظاهر إطلاقه أنه لا فرق في حرمة الإشارة والدلالة بينهما إذا كان للقاتل علم أم لم يكن والراجح أن المنع محمول على ما إذا لم يكن له علم به، والأصل في ذلك حديث أبي قتادة أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام حين سألوه عن لحم حمار وحش اصطاده أبو قتادة: قال: هل منكم أحد أمره أو أشار إليه؟ قالوا: "لا"، قال: فكلوا ما بقي من لحمه"، رواه البخاري ومسلم، علق حله على عدم الإشارة إليه، وكذا الدلالة تزيل الأمن من الصيد فيحرم . [تبيين الحقائق: ٢٥٧/٢] عليه: أي على الصيد، وهي إذا كان الصيد غائباً، ومحل تحريمهما إذا لم يعلم القاتل لا إذا علم. (ط)
And killing game: meaning beware also; because of His saying, exalted: 'And do not kill game while you are in a state of ihram' (al-Ma'idah 5:95), i.e., land game. (T., A.) And pointing to it, and pointing occurs when the game is present. (Ayni) It is conjoined to his saying 'killing game', and the apparent unrestricted nature of it is that there is no difference in the prohibition of pointing and indicating between whether the killer had knowledge or not, and the preponderant view is that the prohibition is restricted to when he does not have knowledge of it. The basis for that is the hadith of Abu Qatada that the Prophet, peace be upon him, when they asked him about the meat of a wild donkey that Abu Qatada had hunted, said: 'Is there anyone among you who commanded him or pointed to him?' They said: 'No.' He said: 'Then eat what remains of its meat.' Narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim. He conditioned its permissibility on the absence of pointing to him. Similarly, indication removes the sense of security from the game, so it is prohibited. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 2:257] 'Alayhi: i.e., to the game, and it is when the game is absent. And the place of their prohibition is when the killer does not know, not when he knows. (T.)
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the prohibition of killing game during ihram. It begins by citing the Quranic verse (al-Ma'idah 5:95) which explicitly forbids hunting land game while in ihram. The commentary then addresses the related acts of pointing to game (when it is present) and indicating its location (when it is absent). The initial apparent ruling from the matn is that both pointing and indicating are absolutely prohibited, regardless of whether the killer had prior knowledge. However, the commentator gives the preponderant (rajih) opinion that the prohibition is limited to cases where the killer does not already know about the game. This is based on the hadith of Abu Qatada, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) asked whether anyone had pointed or gestured to the hunter; when the answer was no, he permitted the meat. The hadith implies that if someone had pointed or indicated, the meat would be forbidden. The text clarifies that pointing is for present game (the hunter can see it) and indication (dalala) is for absent game (the hunter needs guidance). The prohibition applies when the killer is unaware; if he already knows about the game, pointing or indicating does not add a prohibition. This is a characteristic of this issue.

Key Terms
الصيد (al-ṣayd): Land game (terrestrial animals that can be hunted).
الإشارة (al-ishārah): Pointing to game that is present so that the hunter can see it.
الدلالة (ad-dalālah): Indicating the location of game that is absent, guiding the hunter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does pointing to game become prohibited according to the preponderant view in this passage?
A) Always, regardless of the killer's knowledge
B) Only when the killer had no prior knowledge of the game
C) Only when the game is absent
D) Only when the game is present

Key Takeaway
Killing land game during ihram is haram; pointing or indicating game is only prohibited if the hunter was unaware of the game prior to the pointing or indication.

Prohibited Sewn Garments in Ihram: Definition, Evidence, and Exception
Ruling with proof on prohibited sewn garments in ihram, with definition of 'wearing' and exception for khuffs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of 'wearing' (lubs) in ihram, list the prohibited garments, explain the exception for khuffs, and identify the correct location of the cut based on the Hanafi definition of ka'b.

Core Idea
Any garment that drapes over the body and stays on by stitching is prohibited in ihram; only the khuff exception requires cutting below the mid-foot joint.

In this lesson, we examine the detailed ruling on prohibited sewn garments during ihram. The Hanafi school provides a precise definition of what counts as 'wearing' and clarifies the exception for leather socks (khuffs) when sandals are unavailable. We also unpack a unique Hanafi definition of the 'ankle' (ka'b) that affects the required cut.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Wearing sewn garments for men in ihram is haram. The passage focuses on the prohibition.
Women are allowed to wear khuffs; the prohibition is specific to men.
2
Understand the Hanafi definition of 'wearing'
Lubs is defined as any item that is carried on the body or a part of it and stays on by itself through stitching, gluing, or similar means.
This broad definition includes shirts, trousers, turbans, etc.
3
List the prohibited items
The passage enumerates: shirt (including zarwiyah and burnus), trousers, turban, cap, qaba' (when worn with arms inserted), and khuffs (leather socks).
The qaba' is prohibited only when the shoulders and hands go into the sleeves.
4
Note the dual for khuffs and the women's exception
Khuffs are mentioned in the dual because wearing a single khuff is prohibited even outside ihram. Women are exempt from this prohibition.
The exception for khuffs applies only when sandals are unavailable.
5
Study the dalil
The hadith of Ibn Umar (muttafaq 'alayh) explicitly prohibits these garments with an exception for khuffs after cutting them below the ka'b.
The hadith is strong evidence (thubut qati, dalala zanni for the exception).
6
Define the ka'b as used in the exception
According to the Hanafi school, ka'b here means the joint in the middle of the foot where the sandal lace is tied, not the protruding ankle bone.
This definition changes the required cut point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولبس القميص: يدخل فيه الزروية والبرنس والضابط ههنا أن كل شيء محمول على قدر البدن أو بعضه بحيث يستمسك عليه بنفسه بخياطة أو لزق أو غيرهما يكون لبسا، والسراويل أعجمية والجمع سراويلات، وقيل: السراويل جمع سروال والعمامة والقلنسوة؛ لأن لبسهما يوجب ستر الرأس وهو ممنوع وإن كان وسط الرأس مكشوفا، ولبس القباء بالمد بأن يدخل منكبيه ويديه في كميه، فلو لم يدخل جاز كما لو ارتدى بقميص ونحوه، ولبس الخفين وإنما ثني؛ لأن لبس الخف الواحد ممنوع في غير حالة الإحرام أيضاً، وهذا بالنسبة للرجال، أما النساء فيجوز لهن لبس الخفين، والأصل في منع لبس هذه الأشياء حديث ابن عمر لما أنه قال: سئل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ما يلبس المحرم؟ قال: "لا يلبس القميص ولا العمامة ولا البرنس ولا السراويل ولا ما مسه ورس ولا زعفران ولا الخفين، إلا أن لا يجد النعلين فليقطعهما حتى يكونا أسفل من الكعبين متفق عليه والكعب هنا هو المفصل الذي في وسط القدم عند معقد الشراك فيما روى هشام عن محمد تبيين الحقائق: ٢٥٨/٢] (فتح) إلا أن أي واتق لبس الخفين إلا أن لا تجد. (مسكين) الكعبين أي المفصلين الذين وسط القدمين عند معقد شراك النعل، وهو سيره الذي على ظهر القدم، وهو المراد هنا بالكعب. (مسكين)
And wearing the shirt: it includes the zarwiyah and the burnus, and the criterion here is that everything that is carried on the size of the body or a part of it such that it stays on by itself through stitching or glue or otherwise is considered 'wearing'. And the sarawil is a non-Arabic word, plural sarawilat, and it is said: sarawil is plural of sirwal. And the turban and the cap; because wearing them necessitates covering the head, which is prohibited, even if the middle of the head is exposed. And wearing the qaba' with elongation: that he puts his shoulders and hands into its sleeves, so if he does not insert [his hands], it is permissible, as if he wrapped himself in a shirt and the like. And wearing the khuffs (leather socks), and it is dual because wearing a single khuff is prohibited even outside the state of ihram, and this is with respect to men, but women may wear khuffs. The basis for the prohibition of these things is the hadith of Ibn Umar, who said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, was asked: What may the muhrim wear? He said: 'He may not wear the shirt, nor the turban, nor the burnus, nor the trousers, nor anything touched by wars or za'faran, nor the khuffs, unless he cannot find sandals, then let him cut them so that they become below the ankles.' Agreed upon. And the ankle here is the joint that is in the middle of the foot at the point of the shoelace, as related by Hisham from Muhammad. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 2:258] (Fath) The exception: meaning beware of wearing the khuffs unless you cannot find [sandals]. (Miskin) The two ankles: meaning the two joints that are in the middle of the feet at the place where the shoelace of the sandal is tied, and that is the strap on the top of the foot, and that is what is meant here by the ankle. (Miskin)
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling with proof regarding the prohibition of wearing sewn (tailored) garments during ihram. The commentator begins by defining 'wearing' (lubs) as any item that is carried on the body (or part of it) and stays on by itself through stitching, gluing, or similar means. This includes a shirt (qamis), which encompasses garments like the zarwiyah (a type of shirt) and burnus (hooded cloak). The sarawil (trousers) is a Persian word; its plural is sarawilat. The turban and cap (qalansuwa) are prohibited because they cover the head, even if the crown is exposed. The qaba' (a long outer garment) is considered 'worn' when one inserts his shoulders and arms into its sleeves; if he does not insert his arms (e.g., draping it over), it is permissible. The khuffs (leather socks) are mentioned in the dual form because wearing a single khuff is prohibited even outside ihram. Women are allowed to wear khuffs. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them) in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) enumerated the prohibited garments, including the exception for khuffs: if the muhrim cannot find sandals, he may wear khuffs after cutting them below the ankles. The 'ankle' (ka'b) here is defined as the joint in the middle of the foot where the shoelace of the sandal is tied, not the protruding ankle bone commonly understood. This is based on a transmission from Muhammad al-Shaybani. The commentary also repeats the exception condition.

Key Terms
اللبس (al-lubs): Wearing in the sense of an item that is carried on the body and stays on by itself via stitching, gluing, etc.
الكعب (al-ka'b): The joint in the middle of the foot at the point of the shoelace strap, not the protruding ankle bone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is sewn.
B) It is carried on the body and stays by itself.
C) It covers the body.
D) It is made of cloth.

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of sewn garments in ihram is based on a clear hadith, with an exception for khuffs cut below the unique Hanafi definition of ka'b (mid-foot joint).

Prohibition of Dyed Garments: 'Usfur Dispute and the Exception of Washing
Inter-madhhab dispute on 'usfur with Hanafi reliance on smell.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on garments dyed with wars, saffron, or safflower, explain the exception for washed garments, and evaluate the Shafi'i/Hanbali counter-position regarding 'usfur.

Core Idea
A muhrim cannot wear a garment dyed with perfume; only if washed and scent- and color-free is it allowed.

In this passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq, we learn that the muhrim must avoid not only obvious perfumes but also garments dyed with certain plant-based dyes that carry fragrance. The key issue is whether safflower ('usfur) is considered a perfume — the Hanafis say yes, the Shafi'is and Hanbalis say no. The text also carves out an exception: if the garment is thoroughly washed so that no dye transfers and no scent remains, wearing it becomes permissible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited substances
List the three dyes mentioned: wars (a Yemeni plant), saffron, and safflower ('usfur). Note their common feature: they all have a fragrant quality.
Wars and saffron are uncontroversial; the dispute is over 'usfur.
2
Understand the exception
The text says 'except if it is washed so that it does not yanfud.' Yanfud can mean either shedding dye or emitting fragrance. The Hanafi school relies on the smell: if any fragrance remains, the prohibition still applies.
Imam Muhammad says either transfer of color or emission of fragrance suffices to prohibit.
3
Note the inter-madhhab dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad permit wearing garments dyed with 'usfur because they do not consider it a perfume. The Hanafi school prohibits it, requiring expiation if worn deliberately.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; each school has its evidence.
4
Analyze the two interpretations of نفض (nafd)
Some jurists define nafd as shedding of dye particles; others as emanation of perfume smell. The text states the relied-upon view is the smell. Muhammad's view combines both conditions as alternative triggers.
The practical effect: if the garment has no smell but the dye transfers, it is prohibited according to Muhammad.
5
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
For a Hanafi, wearing an unwashed safflower-dyed garment invalidates a specific act and requires dam. For a Shafi'i, it is permissible and no penalty is due.
This difference affects how a mufti advises a muhrim today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثوب المصبوغ بورس أو زعفران أو عصفر، بورس: نبات كالسمسم ليس إلا باليمن، يزرع فيبقى نحو عشرين سنة. (قاموس) أو عصفر وهو زهر القرطم، وقال الشافعي وأحمد: لا بأس بلبس المعصفر ؛ لأنه لا طيب له رمز الحقائق: ١٥٣/١] إلا أن يكون غسيلاً لا ينفض وستر الرأس والوجه وغسلهما بالخطمي، ومس الطيب، أي واتق أيضاً أن يكون غسيلاً: أي الثوب المصبوغ بأحد هذه الأشياء. (ط) لا ينفض [ أي لا يفوح، وقيل: لا يتناثر وهو أقرب لمادة اللفظ (عيني) بضم الفاء، والنفض تناثر الصبغ عند الفقهاء والتعويل على الرائحة، حتى لو كان لا يتناثر لكن يفوح ريحه يمنع منه المحرم كالثوب المبخر، وقيل: النفض: فوحان الطيب، وهو الأصح، وعند محمد: أحد الأمرين إما أن يتعدى أثر الصبغ إلى غيره وإن لم يفح، أو يفوح وإن لم يتعد أثر الصبغ إلى غيره. (فتح)
And the garment dyed with wars, or saffron, or safflower. Wars: a plant like sesame, only in Yemen, it is planted and remains for about twenty years. (Qamus) Or safflower, which is the flower of the safflower plant. And al-Shafi'i and Ahmad said: There is no harm in wearing the safflower-dyed garment, because it has no perfume. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1:153) Except if it is washed so that it does not 'yanfud' (emit fragrance or shed dye). And covering the head and face, and washing them with khitmi, and touching perfume. Meaning: beware also that it be washed: i.e., the garment dyed with one of these things. (T.) 'La yanfud' [meaning: it does not emit fragrance, and it is said: it does not shed, and that is closer to the wording (Ayni) with damma on the fa, and 'nafd' is the shedding of dye according to the jurists, but reliance is on the smell, so even if it does not shed but its smell emanates, the muhrim is prevented from it like a perfumed garment. And it is said: 'nafd' means the emanation of perfume, and that is the most correct. According to Muhammad: one of two matters either that the effect of the dye transfers to another even if it does not emit, or it emits even if its effect does not transfer to another. (Fath)
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage covers the prohibition of wearing garments dyed with wars (a plant from Yemen resembling sesame), saffron (za'faran), or safflower ('usfur). The commentary defines these substances and then presents an inter-madhhab dispute: Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad permit wearing garments dyed with 'usfur because it is not a perfume, while the Hanafi school prohibits it. The text then states the exception: if the garment is washed such that it no longer 'yanfud' (the dye does not shed or the fragrance does not emanate), then it is permissible. The commentator explains two interpretations of 'yanfud': (1) it does not shed dye, or (2) it does not emit fragrance. The correct view according to some is that reliance is on smell; if the garment still smells perfumed, it is prohibited even if it doesn't shed. According to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, either one of two conditions (transfer of dye or emission of fragrance) triggers the prohibition. The passage also mentions the subsequent prohibitions of covering the head/face and using perfume, which are part of the matn but the commentary continues on the next page.

Key Terms
الورس (al-wars): A plant like sesame, found in Yemen, used as a dye and perfume.
العصفر (al-ʿusfur): Safflower, the flower of the safflower plant, used as a dye.
النفض (an-nafḍ): Shedding of dye or emission of fragrance; the relied-upon meaning is the emanation of perfume smell.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Only if it is not washed

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits garments dyed with any perfume, including safflower, unless they are washed and free of both scent and color transfer.
