Ruling of Tawaf al-Qudum: Sunnah for Non-Makkans
Inter-madhhab dispute on Tawaf al-Qudum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Tawaf al-Qudum and explain the linguistic basis for why it is sunnah rather than wajib, while also articulating the opposing view of Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Qudum is a voluntary greeting to the House, not an obligation.

This lesson examines the ruling of Tawaf al-Qudum (arrival tawaf) — the circumambulation performed upon entering Mecca for Hajj or Umrah. The Hanafi school holds it is a commendable sunnah for non-Makkans, while Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad consider it wajib. The core of the dispute lies in how the Prophet's command 'let him greet it with tawaf' is interpreted. We will trace the linguistic analysis that leads the Hanafis to the sunnah ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is Tawaf al-Qudum? According to the Hanafi school, what is its hukm and for whom?
The text explicitly says it is sunnah for non-Makkans.
2
Locate the opposing dalil
What evidence do Malik and Ahmad use to claim it is wajib? Identify the hadith and the reasoning.
The hadith contains an imperative (amr) which in usul indicates obligation.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school rebut the wajib claim? Focus on the word 'tahiyya' and the linguistic analysis.
The Prophet called it a greeting, which is voluntary initiation.
4
Understand the analogy
The Hanafis analogize Tawaf al-Qudum to tahiyyat al-masjid. Explain this analogy and why it supports the sunnah ruling.
Both are recommended acts of greeting.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference between the two positions? Does omitting it incur sin?
For Hanafis, no sin; for Malik and Ahmad, sin unless excused.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
للقدوم متعلق بقوله : "طف" أي فطف مضطبعا سبعة أشواط لأجل طواف القدوم. (عيني) سنة لغير المكي: [لأن القدوم يتحقق في حق دون ساكن مكة، ويندب له بعد ذلك الالتزام بالملتزم والشرب من ماء زمزم (ط) (مسكين] لأنه على من يقدم والمكي لا يقدم؛ لأن أهل مكة في حق طواف القدوم كالجالس في المسجد في حق تحية المسجد، ويقال لطواف القدوم طواف التحية واللقاء أيضاً، وقال مالك وأحمد: طواف القدوم واجب؛ لقوله عليه: "من أتى البيت فليحيه بالطواف" أمر وهو للوجوب، ولنا: أنه عليها سماه تحية بقوله: "فليحيه" فلا يفيد الوجوب؛ لأن التحية في اللغة اسم للإكرام يبدأ به الإنسان على سبيل التبرع، ولا يلزم وجوب رد السلام بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذَا حُيِّيتُمْ بِتَحِيَّةٍ فَحَيُّوا بِأَحْسَنَ مِنْهَا أَوْ رُدُّوهَا﴾ (النساء: ٨٦)؛ لأنه ليس بابتداء إحسان، وإنما هو مجازاة للسلام الأول. رمز الحقائق: ١٥٦/١]
For the arrival is related to his saying: 'perform tawaf', i.e., perform tawaf with idtiba' seven circuits for the sake of tawaf of arrival. (Ayni) It is sunnah for non-Makkan: [because arrival is realized in regard to one who comes, not a resident of Mecca, and he is recommended after that to cling to the Multazam and drink from Zamzam water. (T) (Miskin) because it is for one who arrives, and the Makkan does not arrive; for the people of Mecca regarding tawaf of arrival are like the one sitting in the mosque regarding tahiyyat al-masjid. It is also called tawaf of greeting and meeting. Malik and Ahmad said: Tawaf of arrival is wajib, based on his saying: 'Whoever comes to the House, let him greet it with tawaf' - a command which indicates obligation. Our evidence: He called it greeting by saying 'let him greet it', so it does not indicate obligation, because greeting in language is a term for honor that one initiates voluntarily, and the obligation of returning greeting by the verse 'And when you are greeted with a greeting, greet with better than it or return it' (4:86) is not similar, because it is not initiating a favor but rather reciprocating the first greeting. Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 156/1.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage specifically addresses the ruling of tawaf al-qudum (arrival tawaf). It is an inter-madhhab dispute because it contrasts the Hanafi position with that of Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal. The text begins by explaining that the phrase 'for the arrival' in the matn (original text of Kanz al-Daqa'iq) refers to tawaf performed upon arriving in Mecca. According to the Hanafi school, this tawaf is sunnah for non-Makkans only. The reason is that 'arrival' is only realized for someone coming from outside; a resident of Mecca does not 'arrive' in the sense of entering the city. It is analogous to the tahiyyat al-masjid (greeting the mosque) prayer for one who enters a mosque—it is recommended but not obligatory. Indeed, tawaf al-qudum is also called tawaf al-tahiyya (greeting) and tawaf al-liqa' (meeting). This is in contrast to Malik and Ahmad, who hold that tawaf al-qudum is wajib. Their evidence is the hadith: 'Whoever comes to the House, let him greet it with tawaf.' They argue that the imperative form (amr) indicates obligation. The Hanafi response is subtle but decisive: the Prophet himself called it a 'greeting' (tahiyya). In the Arabic language, a greeting (tahiyya) is a voluntary act of honor that one initiates, not an obligatory duty. The Quranic command to return a greeting (in Surah al-Nisa) is not a counterexample because it is a reciprocation of an initial greeting, not an initiation. Therefore, the command 'let him greet it' is interpreted as a recommendation (nadb), not an obligation. This shows the Hanafi reliance on linguistic analysis and the principle that an imperative can be for recommendation if the context indicates, especially when the action is called 'greeting' which inherently implies voluntariness.

Key Terms
طواف القدوم (ṭawāf al-qudūm): The circumambulation performed upon arrival in Mecca, before the obligatory tawaf, especially for those coming from outside.
تحية المسجد (taḥiyyat al-masjid): Two rak'at of greeting when entering a mosque; considered sunnah by all schools except Hanbalis who require it as wajib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence the Hanafi school uses to argue that Tawaf al-Qudum is sunnah rather than wajib?
A) The hadith does not exist in strong collections.
B) The Prophet called it a 'greeting' (tahiyya), which is voluntary.
C) Ijma of the Companions.
D) The verse about returning greetings (4:86).

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Qudum is a sunnah act of greeting for non-Makkans; its omission is not sinful in the Hanafi school due to the linguistic interpretation of 'tahiyya'.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Procedure of Sa'i between Safa and Marwah
Description of Sa'i steps with rulings and a dispute on counting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the steps of Sa'i according to the Hanafi school and identify the ruling on ascending the hills and the counting of rounds.

Core Idea
Sa'i consists of seven legs between Safa and Marwah, each leg a separate round, ending at Marwah; ascending the hills is Sunnah.

This passage details the ritual of Sa'i, from standing on Safa to completing seven rounds. It highlights the Sunnah of ascending the hills and addresses a dispute about whether each leg or each round-trip counts as a round. Understanding these rulings ensures correct performance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the starting point and initial actions
Note that the pilgrim begins at Safa, faces the Kaaba, and performs takbir, tahlil, salawat, and du'a.
2
Trace the movement between the hills
The pilgrim descends towards Marwah, walking normally until the middle of the valley, then runs between the two green markers. Upon reaching Marwah, he repeats the actions done on Safa.
This completes one round (Shawt) according to the Hanafi school.
3
Count the rounds correctly
Each leg (Safa to Marwah and back) counts as a separate round, so seven rounds end at Marwah. Note the dispute with some Shafi'is who count each round-trip as one round.
The Hadith that the Prophet's last round ended at Marwah supports the Hanafi position.
4
Assess the rulings on ascending the hills
Ascending Safa and Marwah is Sunnah; omitting it is disliked (makruh) but does not invalidate the Sa'i.
5
Review the du'a during the run
The pilgrim should say the specific supplication while running between the markers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اخرج إلى الصفا وقم عليه مستقبل البيت مكبراً مهللاً مصلياً على النبي داعياً ربك لحاجتك، ثم اهبط نحو المروة ساعياً بين الميلين الأخضرين، وافعل عليها فعلك على الصفا، وطف بينهما سبعة أشواط تبدأ بالصفا وتختم بالمروة. وقد روي أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم صعد على الصفا حتى إذا نظر إلى البيت قام مستقبلاً للبيت. والصعود على الصفا والمروة سنة ولا شيء عليه لو ترك الصعود بل يكره. وينبغي أن يمشي على هيئته حتى يدخل بطن الوادي، ثم يسعى بين الميلين الأخضرين، وهما علامتان لموضع الهرولة في بطن الوادي. وإذا أخذ المحرم في السعي بينهما يقول: رب اغفر وارحم وتجاوز عما تعلم إنك أنت الأعز الأكرم. واختلف في الشوط: فالذهاب من الصفا إلى المروة شوط، والعود من المروة إلى الصفا شوط آخر، هكذا حتى يتم السبعة على المروة. وقال الطحاوي وبعض الشافعية: الذهاب والإياب شوط واحد قياساً على الطواف، ويرد عليهم بما روي أن آخر طوافه كان على المروة، والشوط في الطواف لا يتم إلا بالحجر الأسود، وفي السعي يتم بالمروة.
Then go out to as-Safa and stand upon it facing the House, saying 'Allahu Akbar', 'La ilaha illallah', sending blessings on the Prophet, and supplicating your Lord for your need. Then descend towards al-Marwah, hastening between the two green milestones, and do upon it as you did on as-Safa. And pace between them seven rounds, beginning at as-Safa and ending at al-Marwah. It is related that the Prophet (peace be upon him) ascended as-Safa until when he looked at the House, he stood facing it. Ascending as-Safa and al-Marwah is Sunnah; there is nothing upon him if he leaves it, but it is disliked. He should walk in his normal gait until he enters the middle of the valley, then he runs between the two green milestones, which are two markers for the place of jogging in the valley. When the pilgrim begins running between them, he says: 'O Lord, forgive, have mercy, and overlook what You know; indeed You are the Most Mighty, the Most Generous.' There is a difference of opinion concerning the round: going from as-Safa to al-Marwah is one round, and returning from al-Marwah to as-Safa is another round, thus until completing seven rounds at al-Marwah. At-Tahawi and some Shafi'is say that going and returning is one round, by analogy with Tawaf around the House, but this is refuted by the narration that his last Tawaf was at al-Marwah, and a round in Tawaf is not completed except at the Black Stone, while in Sa'i it is completed at al-Marwah.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage describes the procedure of Sa'i between Safa and Marwah. It begins with standing on Safa facing the Kaaba, glorifying Allah, sending blessings on the Prophet, and making du'a. Then descending towards Marwah, walking normally until the middle of the valley, then running (hastening) between the two green milestones, which mark the area of jogging. Upon reaching Marwah, the pilgrim does the same as on Safa. This constitutes one round. The pilgrim performs seven rounds, starting at Safa and ending at Marwah. The text notes that ascending the hills is Sunnah, and there is no sin in leaving it, though it is disliked. A dispute is mentioned regarding the counting of rounds: according to the Hanafi school, each leg (Safa to Marwah and Marwah to Safa) counts as a separate round, totaling seven rounds ending at Marwah. At-Tahawi and some Shafi'is consider the going and returning as one round, analogizing to Tawaf, but this is rejected based on the hadith that the Prophet's last round ended at Marwah, and the difference in the completion point.

Key Terms
الصفا والمروة (as-Safa wa al-Marwah): Two small hills near the Kaaba in Mecca, between which the Sa'i is performed.
السعي (as-Sa'i): The ritual walking or hastening between Safa and Marwah seven times during Hajj or Umrah.
الميلان الأخضران (al-Meelan al-Akhdaran): Two green markers in the middle of the valley where the pilgrim runs (harwalah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many rounds constitute the Sa'i between Safa and Marwah?
A) Four rounds, starting at Marwah
B) Seven rounds, starting at Safa and ending at Marwah
C) Seven rounds, starting at Marwah and ending at Safa
D) Three rounds, each including going and returning

Key Takeaway
The Sa'i must be performed as seven legs (rounds) between Safa and Marwah, starting at Safa and ending at Marwah, with the Sunnah of ascending the hills and running between the green markers.

Ruling of Sa'i: Wajib not Rukn
Inter-madhhab dispute with Qur'anic proof for Sa'i's wajib status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that Sa'i is wajib and distinguish it from the Shafi'i/Maliki view that it is a rukn, citing the dalil and thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Sa'i is wajib, not rukn: omission requires compensation but does not invalidate Hajj.

The act of Sa'i (walking between Safa and Marwah) is a central rite of Hajj and Umrah, but its precise legal status is disputed. The Hanafi school holds that it is wajib—an obligation whose omission can be compensated—while other schools consider it a rukn whose omission nullifies the pilgrimage. This lesson examines the evidence, focusing on the Qur'anic verse that shapes the Hanafi ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school rules regarding Sa'i: it is wajib, not a rukn. Note the consequence of omission.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i hold Sa'i to be a rukn (pillar). Understand the practical stake: invalidation vs. compensation.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The opponent relies on the hadith: 'Perform Sa'i, for Allah has prescribed it.' Consider why this might suggest pillar-hood.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond with the Qur'anic verse (2:158): the phrase 'no blame' (lā junāḥ) and 'whoever volunteers good' (tatawwa‘a) indicate that the obligation is not at the level of a rukn.
The Hanafi usul principle: a text with zanni dalāla cannot establish a rukn.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: If Sa'i is omitted, the Hanafi school rules the Hajj valid with a dam (sacrifice), whereas the Shafi'i/Maliki school rules the Hajj invalid and requiring repetition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم السعي بين الصفا والمروة واجب عندنا وقال مالك والشافعي ركن لقوله عليه السلام: 'اسعوا فإن الله كتب عليكم السعي'، ولنا قوله تعالى: {إِنَّ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةَ مِنْ شَعَائِرِ اللَّهِ فَمَنْ حَجَّ الْبَيْتَ أَوِ اعْتَمَرَ فَلَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ يَطَّوَّفَ بِهِمَا وَمَنْ تَطَوَّعَ خَيْرًا فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ شَاكِرٌ عَلِيمٌ} (البقرة:158). فرفع الجناح والتخيير ينفي الفرضية والركنية. ويستحب له إذا فرغ من السعي أن يصلي ركعتين في المسجد ودخول البيت إذا لم يؤذ أحدا، ويقصد مصلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قبل وجهه وجعل الباب قبل ظهره، حتى يكون بينه وبين الجدار الذي قبل وجهه نحو ثلاثة أذرع، ثم يصلي فإذا صلى إلى الجدار المذكور يضع خده عليه، ويستغفر الله ويحمده، ثم يأتي الأركان فيحمد ويهلل ويسبح ويكبر ويسأل الله ما شاء، ويلزم الأدب ما استطاع بظاهره وباطنه.
Then the Sa'i between Safa and Marwah is wajib (obligatory) according to us, while Malik and ash-Shafi'i say it is a rukn (pillar), due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Perform Sa'i, for Allah has prescribed Sa'i upon you.' Our proof is the saying of Allah Almighty: {Indeed, as-Safa and al-Marwah are among the symbols of Allah. So whoever makes Hajj to the House or performs 'Umrah, there is no blame upon him to walk between them. And whoever volunteers good, then indeed Allah is Appreciative and Knowing.} (al-Baqarah:158). Thus the removal of blame and the option negate obligation and pillar-hood. And it is recommended for him, when he finishes the Sa'i, to pray two rak'ahs in the mosque and to enter the House if it does not harm anyone, and to head towards the prayer place of the Prophet (peace be upon him) with his face in front and making the door behind his back, until there is about three cubits between him and the wall in front of his face, then he prays. When he prays facing the mentioned wall, he places his cheek on it, seeks forgiveness from Allah and praises Him, then goes to the corners, praising, saying 'La ilaha illallah', 'Subhanallah', 'Allahu Akbar', and asks Allah whatever he wishes. And he adheres to proper conduct as much as possible outwardly and inwardly.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This section addresses the legal ruling of Sa'i. The Hanafi school holds that Sa'i is wajib (obligatory) but not a rukn (pillar) of Hajj or Umrah. The opposing view of Imam Malik and Imam ash-Shafi'i is that it is a rukn, meaning that omitting it invalidates the Hajj. The Hanafi proof is from the Quranic verse (2:158) which says 'there is no blame upon him to walk between them.' The phrase 'no blame' (la junah) indicates that it is not mandatory to the degree of pillar-hood; rather, it is a recommended or obligatory act that does not cause major deficiency if omitted, though one must compensate. The verse uses the word 'tatawwa'a' (volunteers good), implying optionality. After the Sa'i, the text lists recommended post-Sa'i actions: praying two rak'ahs in the mosque, entering the Kaaba if possible, visiting the Prophet's prayer spot, and making du'a and dhikr at the corners.

Key Terms
الواجب (al-wajib): An obligatory act that is not at the level of fard; omission requires compensation but does not invalidate the act.
الركن (ar-rukn): A pillar or integral part of an act; omission invalidates the act.
الجناح (al-junah): Blame or sin; its negation indicates the act is not obligatory at the highest level.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school consider Sa'i to be wajib and not a rukn?
A) Because the Prophet said 'As if Sa'i were not obligatory'
B) Because the Qur'an says 'There is no blame' and 'whoever volunteers good', indicating it is not at the level of pillar
C) Because the Sahaba agreed it is sunnah
D) Because Qiyas shows it is like Tawaf, which is wajib

Key Takeaway
Sa'i is wajib in Hajj and Umrah according to the Hanafi school; omission requires compensation (dam) but does not invalidate the pilgrimage.

Rulings on Staying in Ihram and Performing Voluntary Tawaf
Rulings on staying in Ihram and performing voluntary Tawaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings on staying in Makkah in Ihram after Sa'i, identify the rules for voluntary Tawaf, and apply the conditions when interrupting Tawaf for congregational prayer.

Core Idea
Voluntary Tawaf is allowed but no Sa'i or Ramal after it; if prayer starts, join then resume.

After completing the Sa'i, the pilgrim remains in Ihram in Makkah until the 8th of Dhul Hijjah. During this waiting period, one may perform voluntary Tawaf, but with specific rules: no Sa'i follows these Tawafs, no Ramal is done, and if congregational prayer begins, the Tawaf must be interrupted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on staying
The text commands: 'Then stay in Makkah in Ihram.' Recognize that this is obligatory (wajib) because one is in Ihram for Hajj and cannot exit before completing rituals.
2
Understand voluntary Tawaf
The text says 'perform Tawaf around the House whenever it occurs to you.' This indicates it is permissible (nafl) to perform Tawaf multiple times.
Tawaf is a virtuous act.
3
Learn the rule of interrupting Tawaf for prayer
If congregational prayer is established while in Tawaf or Sa'i, one must stop and join the prayer, then resume from where left off.
Prayer takes precedence over supererogatory Tawaf.
4
Note the prohibition of Sa'i and Ramal
No Sa'i is performed after these voluntary Tawafs because Sa'i is obligatory only once. Ramal is also not done because it is only legislated for the Tawaf followed by Sa'i.
Even if Sa'i is delayed, the initial Tawaf al-Qudum does not include Ramal.
5
Recognize the prayer after Tawaf
After completing seven rounds (one Tawaf), pray two rak'ahs. This applies to each voluntary Tawaf.
The prayer is sunnah mu'akkadah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم أقم بمكة حراما، وطف بالبيت كلما بدا لك، ثم اخطب قبل يوم التروية. أي امكث بها في حالة الإحرام إلى ثامن ذي الحجة إن كان قدومك قبل ذلك؛ لأنك محرم بالحج، فلا تحلل قبل الإتيان بأفعاله. أقم بمكة أي بعد الفراغ من السعي. وطف بالبيت: ولو أقيمت وهو يطوف أو يسعى ترك ذلك وصلى ثم بنى. واعلم أنه لا يسعى عقب هذه الأطوفة؛ لأن السعي لا يجب إلا مرة واحدة والتنفل به غير مشروع، ولا يرمل في هذه الأطوفة؛ لأن الرمل لم يشرع إلا مرة واحدة في طواف بعده سعي، وكذا إن أخر السعي إلى طواف الزيارة لا يرمل في طواف القدوم أيضاً، ويصلي لكل أسبوع ركعتين. ثم اخطب: أي بعد الزوال وصلاة الظهر خطبة واحدة، ولو خطب قبل الزوال جاز وكره، فيبدأ فيها بالتكبير ثم التلبية ثم التحميد، وفي الحج ثلاث خطب أولها هذه يوم السابع من ذي الحجة، والثانية بعرفات يوم عرفة التاسع من ذي الحجة، والثالثة بمنى في اليوم الحادي عشر، فيفصل بين كل خطبتين بيوم وهذه الخطبة والثالثة خطبة واحدة، ولا يجلس في وسطهما، وخطبة يوم عرفة خطبتان يجلس بينهما، ووقت الأولى والثالثة بعد صلاة الظهر بعد الزوال، ووقت خطبة عرفة بعد الزوال قبل أن يصلي الظهر. وقال زفر: يخطب في ثلاثة أيام متوالية: أولها يوم التروية وآخرها يوم النحر؛ لأنها أيام الموسم ومجتمع الناس. ولنا: أنه عليه السلام خطب في اليوم السابع، وكذا أبو بكر. ولأن المقصود منها التعليم ويوم التروية ويوم النحر اشتغال بأفعال الحج فكان ما ذكرنا أنفع وأشد تأثيراً في القلوب. وإنما سمي يوم التروية؛ لأن الحاج يروون فيه بالماء من العطش بمنى، وروي أن إبراهيم عليه السلام رأى ليلة التروية كأن قائلاً يقول: إن الله يأمر بذبح ابنك هذا، فلما أصبح روى في ذلك من الصباح إلى الرواح أمن الله هذا أم من الشيطان، فمن ثم سمي يوم التروية.
Then stay in Makkah in a state of Ihram, and perform Tawaf around the House whenever it occurs to you. Then deliver the Khutbah before the Day of Tarwiyah. i.e. remain there in the state of Ihram until the eighth of Dhul Hijjah if your arrival was before that, because you are in Ihram for Hajj, so do not exit Ihram before performing its actions. 'Aqim bi Makkah' means after finishing the Sa'i. 'Tuf bi al-bayt': even if the prayer is established while he is performing Tawaf or Sa'i, he leaves that and prays, then builds upon what he did. And know that he does not perform Sa'i after these Tawafs, because Sa'i is only obligatory once and performing it supererogatorily is not legislated. And he does not do Ramal in these Tawafs, because Ramal is only legislated once in a Tawaf followed by Sa'i. Likewise, if he delays Sa'i to Tawaf al-Ziyarah, he does not do Ramal in Tawaf al-Qudum either. And he prays two rak'ahs for every seven rounds. Then deliver the Khutbah: i.e. after Zawal (noon) and after praying Dhuhr, one Khutbah. If he delivers it before Zawal, it is permissible but disliked. He begins it with Takbir, then Talbiyah, then Tahmid. In Hajj, there are three Khutbahs: the first is this one on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah, the second is at 'Arafat on the Day of 'Arafah (9th), and the third is at Mina on the 11th day. Between every two Khutbahs there is a day. The first and third Khutbahs are single Khutbahs without sitting in between, while the Khutbah on the Day of 'Arafah consists of two Khutbahs with sitting between them. The time of the first and third is after Dhuhr prayer after Zawal, while the time of the 'Arafah Khutbah is after Zawal before praying Dhuhr. Zufar said: He delivers Khutbahs on three consecutive days: the first on the day of Tarwiyah and the last on the day of Nahr, because these are the days of the season and the gathering of people. Our proof: The Prophet (peace be upon him) delivered the Khutbah on the 7th day, and similarly Abu Bakr. Because the purpose is teaching, and on the Day of Tarwiyah and the Day of Nahr people are occupied with the rituals of Hajj, so what we mentioned is more beneficial and more effective on the hearts. The day was called Yawm al-Tarwiyah because the pilgrims give water there to quench thirst at Mina, and it is narrated that Ibrahim (peace be upon him) saw on the night of Tarwiyah as if a caller said: 'Allah commands you to sacrifice this son of yours.' So when morning came, he reflected (rawa) on that from morning to evening whether it was from Allah or from Shaytan, hence it was called Yawm al-Tarwiyah.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage covers two main topics: (1) staying in Makkah after Sa'i while in Ihram, and (2) the Khutbah on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah (Yawm al-Tarwiyah). After completing Sa'i, the pilgrim remains in Ihram and performs Tawaf voluntarily. Tawaf can be done even if congregational prayer is established; one should stop and join the prayer, then resume Tawaf. No Sa'i is performed after these supererogatory Tawafs because Sa'i is only obligatory once. Ramal (jogging) is not done in these Tawafs either. Then on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah after Dhuhr, a single Khutbah is delivered. The text details the three Khutbahs of Hajj: this one, the one at 'Arafah (9th), and the one at Mina (11th). The first and third are single Khutbahs, while the 'Arafah Khutbah consists of two with a sitting. There is a disagreement with Zufar who suggested three consecutive days from Tarwiyah to Nahr, but the Hanafi position is based on the practice of the Prophet and Abu Bakr. The name 'Tarwiyah' is explained: pilgrims water themselves and their animals, and it is linked to Prophet Ibrahim's contemplation about sacrificing his son.

Key Terms
يوم التروية (Yawm al-Tarwiyah): The 8th of Dhul Hijjah, when pilgrims prepare water and begin the Hajj rituals. Also the day of the first Hajj Khutbah (though the Khutbah is on the 7th, the text mentions it before this day).
الخطبة (al-Khutbah): A sermon delivered by the imam during Hajj on specific days.
الرمل (ar-Ramal): Jogging with short steps during Tawaf in the first three rounds, specifically done in Tawaf al-Qudum followed by Sa'i.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Voluntary Tawaf in Makkah during the stay is permitted, but without Sa'i or Ramal, and prayer takes precedence.

The Three Khutbahs of Hajj: Schedule and Fiqh
Rulings on the Khutbah of 7th Dhul Hijjah and the three Khutbahs of Hajj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the three Khutbahs of Hajj, describe the timing and structure of each, and evaluate the intra-madhhab dispute with Zufar.

Core Idea
The first Khutbah is on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah, not the 8th, to avoid conflicting with rituals.

The Khutbah on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah marks the beginning of the Hajj sermons. The passage details that it is delivered after Dhuhr as a single Khutbah, whereas the Khutbah at 'Arafah consists of two with a sitting. The text also presents a disagreement with Zufar, who proposed three consecutive days.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three Khutbahs and their days
The text lists: first on 7th Dhul Hijjah, second on 9th at 'Arafah, third on 11th at Mina. Note that between each pair there is a day gap.
2
Note the time and structure of each
First and third are single Khutbahs after Zawal and Dhuhr. Second is two Khutbahs with a sitting, delivered after Zawal before Dhuhr. The first may be delivered before Zawal but it is disliked.
Timing differs for the 'Arafah Khutbah.
3
Examine the content
The Khutbah begins with Takbir, then Talbiyah, then Tahmid. This is specific to Hajj Khutbahs.
The order is emphasized.
4
Analyze Zufar's objection
Zufar argued for three consecutive days (8th, 9th, 10th) based on the gathering of people. Understand his reasoning.
5
Understand the Hanafi response
The Hanafi proof is the practice of the Prophet and Abu Bakr. Also, the purpose of teaching is better served on the 7th, when pilgrims are free from the rituals of Tarwiyah and Nahr.
This is a tarjih based on benefit.

Then stay in Makkah in a state of Ihram, and perform Tawaf around the House whenever it occurs to you. Then deliver the Khutbah before the Day of Tarwiyah. i.e. remain there in the state of Ihram until the eighth of Dhul Hijjah if your arrival was before that, because you are in Ihram for Hajj, so do not exit Ihram before performing its actions. Between every two Khutbahs there is a day. The first and third Khutbahs are single Khutbahs without sitting in between, while the Khutbah on the Day of 'Arafah consists of two Khutbahs with sitting between them. The time of the first and third is after Dhuhr prayer after Zawal, while the time of the 'Arafah Khutbah is after Zawal before praying Dhuhr. Zufar said: He delivers Khutbahs on three consecutive days: the first on the day of Tarwiyah and the last on the day of Nahr, because these are the days of the season and the gathering of people. Our proof: The Prophet (peace be upon him) delivered the Khutbah on the 7th day, and similarly Abu Bakr. Because the purpose is teaching, and on the Day of Tarwiyah and the Day of Nahr people are occupied with the rituals of Hajj, so what we mentioned is more beneficial and more effective on the hearts. The day was called Yawm al-Tarwiyah because the pilgrims give water there to quench thirst at Mina, and it is narrated that Ibrahim (peace be upon him) saw on the night of Tarwiyah as if a caller said: 'Allah commands you to sacrifice this son of yours.' So when morning came, he reflected (rawa) on that from morning to evening whether it was from Allah or from Shaytan, hence it was called Yawm al-Tarwiyah.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage covers two main topics: (1) staying in Makkah after Sa'i while in Ihram, and (2) the Khutbah on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah (Yawm al-Tarwiyah). After completing Sa'i, the pilgrim remains in Ihram and performs Tawaf voluntarily. Tawaf can be done even if congregational prayer is established; one should stop and join the prayer, then resume Tawaf. No Sa'i is performed after these supererogatory Tawafs because Sa'i is only obligatory once. Ramal (jogging) is not done in these Tawafs either. Then on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah after Dhuhr, a single Khutbah is delivered. The text details the three Khutbahs of Hajj: this one, the one at 'Arafah (9th), and the one at Mina (11th). The first and third are single Khutbahs, while the 'Arafah Khutbah consists of two with a sitting. There is a disagreement with Zufar who suggested three consecutive days from Tarwiyah to Nahr, but the Hanafi position is based on the practice of the Prophet and Abu Bakr. The name 'Tarwiyah' is explained: pilgrims water themselves and their animals, and it is linked to Prophet Ibrahim's contemplation about sacrificing his son.

Key Terms
يوم التروية (Yawm al-Tarwiyah): The 8th of Dhul Hijjah, when pilgrims prepare water and begin the Hajj rituals. Also the day of the first Hajj Khutbah (though the Khutbah is on the 7th, the text mentions it before this day).
الخطبة (al-Khutbah): A sermon delivered by the imam during Hajj on specific days.
الرمل (ar-Ramal): Jogging with short steps during Tawaf in the first three rounds, specifically done in Tawaf al-Qudum followed by Sa'i.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many Khutbahs are delivered during Hajj and on which days?
A) Two: 8th and 9th
B) Two: 9th and 10th
C) Three: 7th, 9th, 11th
D) Three: 8th, 9th, 10th

Key Takeaway
The first Hajj Khutbah is on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah, a single Khutbah after Dhuhr, setting the stage for the rituals.

The Hanafi Ruling on Sa'i: Wajib, Not Fard
Dispute on whether Sa'i is fard or wajib with Quranic proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school classifies Sa'i as wajib rather than fard, using Quranic proof, and describe the practical consequence of omitting Sa'i.

Core Idea
Sa'i is wajib, not fard: the Quran's 'no blame' lifts strict obligation, but omission still requires a dam.

This passage addresses a classical dispute: is Sa'i between Safa and Marwah a fard (integral) act that invalidates Hajj if missed, or a wajib (necessary) act that can be compensated with a sacrifice? The Hanafi school takes the latter view, relying on a subtle Quranic expression. By unpacking the proof, you will understand how the Hanafi distinction between fard and wajib is applied to a concrete ritual.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting positions
What do the two sides claim about Sa'i? One side holds it is fard/rukn; the other (Hanafi) holds it is wajib.
2
Locate the Hanafi proof
Which Quranic verse is cited and what key phrase is used to argue against obligation?
The verse is 2:158; the key phrase is 'la junaha' (no blame).
3
Analyze the linguistic argument
How does the phrase 'no blame' negate obligation? What does the word 'tatawwa' (voluntary good) add?
The removal of blame and the option to volunteer indicate the act is not a binding command.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What happens in practice if someone omits Sa'i according to each side?
Hanafi: Hajj valid + dam; Opposing: Hajj invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لقوله علي: "اسعوا فإن الله كتب عليكم السعي"، ولنا قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةَ مِنْ شَعَائِرِ اللَّهِ فَمَنْ حَجَّ الْبَيْتَ أَوِ اعْتَمَرَ فَلَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ يَطَّوَّفَ بِهِمَا وَمَنْ تَطَوَّعَ خَيْراً فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ شَاكِرٌ عَلِيمٌ﴾ (البقرة:١٥٨) فرفع الجناح والتخيير ينفي الفرضية والركنية.
Due to the saying of 'Ali: 'Perform Sa'i, for Allah has prescribed Sa'i upon you', and for us is the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'Indeed, as-Safa and al-Marwah are among the symbols of Allah. So whoever makes Hajj to the House or performs 'Umrah, there is no blame upon him to walk between them. And whoever volunteers good – then indeed, Allah is Appreciative and Knowing.' (Al-Baqarah:158). So the removal of blame and the option negate obligation and integrality.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi proof that Sa'i between Safa and Marwah is wajib (necessary) but not fard (obligatory) and not a rukn (integral). The opposing view (attributed to 'Ali and others) holds it is fard based on the command 'Perform Sa'i'. The Hanafi response cites the Quranic verse which uses the expression 'no blame upon him' and gives an option, which indicates it is not a mandatory obligation. In Hanafi fiqh, wajib is a category below fard; the ruling here is mufta bihi. The verse shows that performing Sa'i is a good act, but not individually binding.

Key Terms
السعي (al-sa'y): The act of walking between the hills of Safa and Marwah during Hajj or Umrah.
الفرضية (al-fardiyyah): The status of being an obligatory (fard) act that must be performed; omission invalidates the Hajj.
الركنية (al-ruknīyah): The status of being an integral part (rukn) of the ritual; omission invalidates the act completely.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis consider Sa'i between Safa and Marwah as wajib and not fard?
A) Because the Quran says 'no blame upon him', indicating it is optional.
B) Because it is proven by a hadith that is not mutawatir.
C) Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed it only once.
D) Because the Quranic verse uses the word 'tatawwa' (voluntary good).

Key Takeaway
Sa'i is wajib in the Hanafi school; omission requires a dam but does not invalidate Hajj.

8 min
Recommended Acts after Sa'i
List of sunnan and mustahabbat after Sa'i with commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the recommended acts after Sa'i and describe how to perform each one.

Core Idea
After Sa'i, pray two rak'ahs, enter the Kaaba if possible, and make supplication at its corners.

Sa'i is a vital rite of Hajj and Umrah. Once completed, the pilgrim should engage in prescribed acts to maximize spiritual benefit. This lesson explains the sunnan acts recommended after Sa'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main recommended acts
Read the source to list the actions: praying two rak'ahs, entering the Kaaba (if no harm), visiting the Prophet's prayer place, and supplicating at the corners.
Also note the additional commentary on Sa'i in the valley.
2
Understand the specific location and posture for prayer
The source describes facing the Prophet's prayer place with the door behind, about three cubits from the wall.
This location is near the Maqam Ibrahim today.
3
Learn the etiquette at the Kaaba corners
After prayer, touch the cheek to the wall, seek forgiveness, praise Allah, then go to each corner making dhikr and du'a.
Maintain inward and outward adab.
4
Note the method of Sa'i in the valley
The commentary by Fath instructs walking briskly between the two green markers in the bottom of the valley.
This is specific to Sa'i, not after it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستحب له إذا فرغ من السعي أن يصلي ركعتين في المسجد ودخول البيت إذا لم يؤذ أحدا، ويقصد مصلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قبل وجهه وجعل الباب قبل ظهره، حتى يكون بينه وبين الجدار الذي قبل وجهه نحو ثلاثة أذرع، ثم يصلي فإذا صلى إلى الجدار المذكور يضع خده عليه، ويستغفر الله ويحمده، ثم يأتي الأركان فيحمد ويهلل ويسبح ويكبر ويسأل الله ما شاء، ويلزم الأدب ما استطاع بظاهره وباطنه. (فتح) بالمروة: وتسعى في بطن الوادي بين الميلين في كل شوط . (ط) ثم أقم بمكة : [ أي بعد الفراغ من السعي (ع)] أي امكث بها في حالة الإحرام إلى ثامن ذي الحجة إن كان قدومك قبل ذلك؛ لأنك محرم بالحج، فلا تحلل قبل الإتيان بأفعاله، وفيه إيماء إلى أنه لا يجوز له أن يفسخ الحج بالعمرة، أما أمره عليها بذلك أصحابه إلا الهدي فمخصوص بهم أو منسوخ، وقوله: طف بالبيت ولو أقيمت وهو يطوف أو يسعى ترك ذلك وصلى ثم بنى، واعلم أنه لا يسعى عقب هذه الأطوفة؛ لأن السعي لا يجب إلا مرة واحدة والتنفل به غير مشروع، ولا يرمل في هذه الأطوفة؛ لأن الرمل لم يشرع إلا مرة واحدة في طواف بعده سعي، وكذا إن أخر السعي إلى طواف الزيارة لا يرمل في طواف القدوم أيضاً، ويصلي لكل أسبوع ركعتين. (فتح) بدا لك: لأنه يشبه الصلاة، وهي خير مود موضوع فكذا الطواف، وهو أفضل الصلاة من في حق الآفاقي وبالعكس للمكي. (ع) أيضاً من ساق: ثم اخطب: أي بعد الزوال والصلاة خطبة واحدة، ولو خطب قبل الزوال جاز وكره، فيبدأ فيها بالتكبير ثم التلبية ثم التحميد.
It is recommended for him, when he finishes the Sa'i, to pray two rak'ahs in the mosque and to enter the House (Kaaba) if he does not harm anyone. He should head to the prayer place of the Prophet (peace be upon him) facing his face and placing the door behind his back, until there is about three cubits between him and the wall that is in front of his face, then pray. When he prays facing the mentioned wall, he places his cheek on it, seeks forgiveness from Allah and praises Him. Then he goes to the corners (of the Kaaba) and praises, says 'La ilaha illallah', glorifies, says 'Allahu Akbar', and asks Allah for whatever he wishes. He must maintain etiquette as much as he can in his outward and inward state. (Fath) at al-Marwah: And he performs Sa'i in the bottom of the valley between the two green markers in each circuit. (T) Then stay in Makkah: i.e., after finishing the Sa'i, remain there in the state of ihram until the eighth of Dhul Hijjah if your arrival was before that, because you are in ihram for Hajj, so do not exit ihram before performing its actions. In this there is an indication that it is not permissible for him to dissolve Hajj into Umrah. As for his (the Prophet's) command to his companions to do that except for those who brought the sacrificial animal, it is specific to them or abrogated. And his saying: 'Perform tawaf of the House' – even if the prayer is established while he is doing tawaf or Sa'i, he leaves that and prays, then continues. And know that he does not perform Sa'i after these tawafs because Sa'i is only obligatory once, and performing it as a supererogatory act is not legislated. And he does not perform raml in these tawafs because raml is only legislated once in a tawaf after which there is Sa'i. Likewise, if he delays the Sa'i until the Tawaf al-Ziyarah, he does not perform raml in the Tawaf al-Qudum either. And he prays two rak'ahs for each seven circuits. (Fath) 'Whenever it appears to you': because it resembles prayer, and prayer is the best of deeds, so likewise tawaf. And it is better than prayer for the one from outside Makkah, and vice versa for the Makkan. (Ayni) Also from Saq: Then deliver a khutbah: i.e., after zawal (noon) and prayer, one khutbah. If he delivers the khutbah before zawal, it is permissible but makruh. He begins it with takbir, then talbiyah, then tahmid.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage details the recommended (mustahabb) acts after completing Sa'i. The pilgrim should pray two rak'ahs in the mosque near the Maqam Ibrahim, enter the Kaaba if possible without causing harm, face the Prophet's prayer spot, and after prayer touch his cheek to the wall, supplicate. Then he goes to the corners of the Kaaba making dhikr. The commentary adds that Sa'i is performed in the bottom of the valley between the two green markers. Then the ruling on staying in Makkah: the pilgrim must remain in ihram until the 8th of Dhul Hijjah; he cannot convert his Hajj to Umrah (tamattu' is for those not bringing a hadi). He should perform tawaf (nafl) whenever he wishes, but if iqamah is called, he must join the congregational prayer and then resume. Note: He does not perform Sa'i after each tawaf because Sa'i is only wajib once. Raml (quick walking) is only done in the first three circuits of the first tawaf that is followed by Sa'i. If Sa'i is delayed to Tawaf al-Ziyarah, then raml is omitted in Tawaf al-Qudum as well. Two rak'ahs are prayed after each seven circuits. The virtue of tawaf is compared to prayer. The heading 'Also from Saq' introduces the next topic on the khutbah. The khutbah on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah is after zawal, one khutbah, with takbir, talbiyah, tahmid.

Key Terms
السعي (al-sa'i): Walking seven times between Safa and Marwah as a rite of Hajj and Umrah.
المصلى (al-musalla): Prayer place; here referring to the spot where the Prophet (ﷺ) prayed near the Kaaba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What condition must be met for entering the Kaaba after Sa'i?
A) You must have a permit.
B) You must not cause harm to anyone.
C) You must be in ihram.
D) You must have performed tawaf first.

Key Takeaway
After Sa'i, engage in prayer, entry into Kaaba if possible, and supplication at the corners with full adab.

Prohibition of Dissolving Hajj into Umrah
Ruling on the illegality of faskh (dissolving Hajj into Umrah)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on dissolving Hajj into Umrah and explain the reason for its prohibition.

Core Idea
Once in Ihram for Hajj, you cannot convert it to Umrah; this is prohibited except for the Prophet's specific command.

After Sa'i, the pilgrim stays in Makkah in ihram. A common question is whether one can change one's intention from Hajj to Umrah. This lesson explains the prohibition of faskh and its basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on dissolving Hajj
Read the part that says 'لا يجوز له أن يفسخ الحج بالعمرة' (it is not permissible for him to dissolve Hajj into Umrah).
This is a clear prohibition.
2
Understand the context
The pilgrim is in ihram for Hajj until the 8th of Dhul Hijjah; they cannot exit ihram before completing Hajj actions.
The text says 'فلا تحلل قبل الإتيان بأفعاله'.
3
Analyze the exception
The Prophet's command to some companions to dissolve was specific to those who did not bring a hadi, or it is abrogated.
So it does not apply to us.
4
Confirm the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school follows the general prohibition; it is not permissible to change Hajj to Umrah.
This is consistent with the Quranic command to complete Hajj and Umrah for Allah.

Source Text

8 min
Rules of Voluntary Tawaf
Rulings on voluntary tawaf during stay in Makkah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the rulings on performing voluntary tawaf while staying in Makkah, including when to leave for prayer, and the prohibition of Sa'i and raml.

Core Idea
Voluntary tawaf is recommended, but no Sa'i or raml is performed after it, and congregational prayer takes precedence.

During the days before Hajj, pilgrims are encouraged to perform voluntary tawaf. However, specific rules apply: Sa'i and raml are not to be repeated, and if the congregational prayer starts, the pilgrim must join it. This lesson explains these rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main rule about leaving tawaf for prayer
The text says: 'if iqamah is called while he is in tawaf or Sa'i, he leaves that and prays, then continues.'
This establishes the priority of congregational prayer.
2
Understand the prohibition of Sa'i after voluntary tawaf
Sa'i is obligatory only once; performing it after a voluntary tawaf is not legislated.
The text says 'لا يسعى عقب هذه الأطوفة؛ لأن السعي لا يجب إلا مرة واحدة والتنفل به غير مشروع'.
3
Learn about raml
Raml (quick walking) is only legislated once in the tawaf that is followed by Sa'i. So it is not done in voluntary tawafs.
If Sa'i is delayed to Tawaf al-Ziyarah, raml is also omitted in Tawaf al-Qudum.
4
Note the virtue of tawaf
The commentary says tawaf is like prayer, and for non-Makkans it is better than prayer.
This encourages voluntary tawaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستحب له إذا فرغ من السعي أن يصلي ركعتين في المسجد ودخول البيت إذا لم يؤذ أحدا، ويقصد مصلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قبل وجهه وجعل الباب قبل ظهره، حتى يكون بينه وبين الجدار الذي قبل وجهه نحو ثلاثة أذرع، ثم يصلي فإذا صلى إلى الجدار المذكور يضع خده عليه، ويستغفر الله ويحمده، ثم يأتي الأركان فيحمد ويهلل ويسبح ويكبر ويسأل الله ما شاء، ويلزم الأدب ما استطاع بظاهره وباطنه. (فتح) بالمروة: وتسعى في بطن الوادي بين الميلين في كل شوط . (ط) ثم أقم بمكة : [ أي بعد الفراغ من السعي (ع)] أي امكث بها في حالة الإحرام إلى ثامن ذي الحجة إن كان قدومك قبل ذلك؛ لأنك محرم بالحج، فلا تحلل قبل الإتيان بأفعاله، وفيه إيماء إلى أنه لا يجوز له أن يفسخ الحج بالعمرة، أما أمره عليها بذلك أصحابه إلا الهدي فمخصوص بهم أو منسوخ، وقوله: طف بالبيت ولو أقيمت وهو يطوف أو يسعى ترك ذلك وصلى ثم بنى، واعلم أنه لا يسعى عقب هذه الأطوفة؛ لأن السعي لا يجب إلا مرة واحدة والتنفل به غير مشروع، ولا يرمل في هذه الأطوفة؛ لأن الرمل لم يشرع إلا مرة واحدة في طواف بعده سعي، وكذا إن أخر السعي إلى طواف الزيارة لا يرمل في طواف القدوم أيضاً، ويصلي لكل أسبوع ركعتين. (فتح) بدا لك: لأنه يشبه الصلاة، وهي خير مود موضوع فكذا الطواف، وهو أفضل الصلاة من في حق الآفاقي وبالعكس للمكي. (ع) أيضاً من ساق: ثم اخطب: أي بعد الزوال والصلاة خطبة واحدة، ولو خطب قبل الزوال جاز وكره، فيبدأ فيها بالتكبير ثم التلبية ثم التحميد.
It is recommended for him, when he finishes the Sa'i, to pray two rak'ahs in the mosque and to enter the House (Kaaba) if he does not harm anyone. He should head to the prayer place of the Prophet (peace be upon him) facing his face and placing the door behind his back, until there is about three cubits between him and the wall that is in front of his face, then pray. When he prays facing the mentioned wall, he places his cheek on it, seeks forgiveness from Allah and praises Him. Then he goes to the corners (of the Kaaba) and praises, says 'La ilaha illallah', glorifies, says 'Allahu Akbar', and asks Allah for whatever he wishes. He must maintain etiquette as much as he can in his outward and inward state. (Fath) at al-Marwah: And he performs Sa'i in the bottom of the valley between the two green markers in each circuit. (T) Then stay in Makkah: i.e., after finishing the Sa'i, remain there in the state of ihram until the eighth of Dhul Hijjah if your arrival was before that, because you are in ihram for Hajj, so do not exit ihram before performing its actions. In this there is an indication that it is not permissible for him to dissolve Hajj into Umrah. As for his (the Prophet's) command to his companions to do that except for those who brought the sacrificial animal, it is specific to them or abrogated. And his saying: 'Perform tawaf of the House' – even if the prayer is established while he is doing tawaf or Sa'i, he leaves that and prays, then continues. And know that he does not perform Sa'i after these tawafs because Sa'i is only obligatory once, and performing it as a supererogatory act is not legislated. And he does not perform raml in these tawafs because raml is only legislated once in a tawaf after which there is Sa'i. Likewise, if he delays the Sa'i until the Tawaf al-Ziyarah, he does not perform raml in the Tawaf al-Qudum either. And he prays two rak'ahs for each seven circuits. (Fath) 'Whenever it appears to you': because it resembles prayer, and prayer is the best of deeds, so likewise tawaf. And it is better than prayer for the one from outside Makkah, and vice versa for the Makkan. (Ayni) Also from Saq: Then deliver a khutbah: i.e., after zawal (noon) and prayer, one khutbah. If he delivers the khutbah before zawal, it is permissible but makruh. He begins it with takbir, then talbiyah, then tahmid.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage details the recommended (mustahabb) acts after completing Sa'i. The pilgrim should pray two rak'ahs in the mosque near the Maqam Ibrahim, enter the Kaaba if possible without causing harm, face the Prophet's prayer spot, and after prayer touch his cheek to the wall, supplicate. Then he goes to the corners of the Kaaba making dhikr. The commentary adds that Sa'i is performed in the bottom of the valley between the two green markers. Then the ruling on staying in Makkah: the pilgrim must remain in ihram until the 8th of Dhul Hijjah; he cannot convert his Hajj to Umrah (tamattu' is for those not bringing a hadi). He should perform tawaf (nafl) whenever he wishes, but if iqamah is called, he must join the congregational prayer and then resume. Note: He does not perform Sa'i after each tawaf because Sa'i is only wajib once. Raml (quick walking) is only done in the first three circuits of the first tawaf that is followed by Sa'i. If Sa'i is delayed to Tawaf al-Ziyarah, then raml is omitted in Tawaf al-Qudum as well. Two rak'ahs are prayed after each seven circuits. The virtue of tawaf is compared to prayer. The heading 'Also from Saq' introduces the next topic on the khutbah. The khutbah on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah is after zawal, one khutbah, with takbir, talbiyah, tahmid.

Key Terms
الطواف (al-tawaf): Circumambulation of the Kaaba seven times; can be obligatory or voluntary.
الرمل (al-raml): Walking quickly with short steps in the first three circuits of tawaf, only in the tawaf followed by Sa'i.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a pilgrim do if the iqamah for Salaat is heard while he is performing voluntary tawaf?
A) Continue the tawaf and pray after.
B) Leave the tawaf, pray, and then continue from the same spot.
C) Abandon the tawaf entirely.
D) Speed up the tawaf to finish before the prayer.

Key Takeaway
When performing voluntary tawaf, join the congregational prayer if called, and do not add Sa'i or raml.
